O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last of the medical sciences together with its fulfilment, and I have made an end by explanations and by its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it for you with this treatise which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to all in all, so its knowledge is lost and destroyed, and nothing remains from the former times except brief descriptions in books which have been passed down by word of mouth.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes error and vanity, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now I believe that I will revive it together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the method of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I shall go on to the forms of instruments for cauterization, and other surgical instruments with their adjustments, explanation, and preparation as may be necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And due to the reason that there are no good master craftsmen found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who embarks on it must surpass others in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he may know the judgment of limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and number of holes (in the skull), and movement, and moving and unmoving veins, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this, Hippocrates says that knowledge with knowledge is a lot, and with practice it becomes little; especially in the art of medicine.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that those who are not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things, beware lest they fall into error and harm people; thus I have often seen many of those who indulge in this discipline without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman and he severed her carotid arteries; thus so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who treated a stone in the bladder of an elderly man and he carried away with him part of his bladder; thus within three days this old man was dead.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and even if they cut it out he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another surgeon who took care of the duke of our land, who had a broken leg with an open wound; and due to their ignorance, the surgeons set the break on top of the wound with strong ligatures, leaving no room for drainage, and left it like that for some time; they commanded him not to untie it; and he stayed like that until his leg became completely swollen and his foot was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and untie his leg; and when I undid it, he found peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nonetheless, corruption was already established in the limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption continued to spread throughout the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And as I saw another wound that was worsening, and then it became inflamed due to the toxicity of its nature.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is caused by a buildup of melancholic humor, it is not advisable to touch it with iron unless it is in such a position that all corrupt matter can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, my dear son, it is necessary for you to know that manual work is divided into two categories: one where there are dangers in various situations, and I will show in each of these places within this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary that you be cautious, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. Take up your arms in repentance, and approach your patients gently yet firmly, and use the best method so that by God's grace you may come to their salvation and be praised; leave behind dreadful diseases with severe suffering; remove from yourself what causes doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the next with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonishments: "Do not take on a severe illness as a cure unless you want to be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and medical cautery, and the chapter is organized from head to toe; it covers instrument shapes, cauterization tools, and everything else necessary for the procedure.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar procedures; this chapter deals with the order of treatment and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar matters; it deals with the head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we recall the work, it is necessary for me to speak of the quality of help and harm in each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest speech and subtlest science and the secret response; many sages have spoken on this, agreeing with each other; I will suffice myself with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery aids universally all complexions where there is matter, be it two complexions: namely hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions with matter, some argued that cautery is a great aid; while others said the opposite: that cautery is not beneficial for illnesses caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness; those who argue otherwise state that cautery provides great relief for hot and dry ailments in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the body of man to its moisture in relation to fire's nature, you find that the former is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let no one interfere except those who have proven it themselves and understand the chapter of cauterization well through long practice, comprehending the diversity of human constitutions, their dispositions, the causes of their illnesses, the circumstances, and the passing of time; we need not fear other constitutions, especially concerning cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that the cautery with fire is one of the secrets of healing and has even greater efficacy than the burning medicinal cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come forth except on the member that is cooked, and it harms no other member unless touched.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines spread from member to another, causing ailments with slow healing; and sometimes kill the patient Fire, due to its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	This I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of speech, as I do not wish to take away from you the secret that is hidden in fire, and the quality of its work, how it drives out bodily ailments, just as the philosopher says in demonstration; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, they agreed upon the time when the cauterizations should be performed, and chose an opportune moment.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is suitable for all times, because it quickly alleviates the harm that may occur; especially if the cauterizations are necessary to alleviate pain or prevent imminent and urgent damage from coming to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think of it, dear son, as the foolish doctor does; for the illness that is healed by cauterization has no relapse; and they say thus: but it is not so as they believe, because cauterization is a medicine that changes the complexion, drying out the humors that are the cause of pain, and is superior to other medicines due to its swift action, and for the power of its work and dominance.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is a significant factor that the disease may arise sometimes according to the patient's constitution and the location of the illness and its nature; and superfluities are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as dental cauterization for pain, and similar things, and that kind of pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth more than medicine, however their intentions are false, and it is cauterization that is the last resort of medicine because when we administer various treatments for any illness and they are ineffective, then we apply cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a golden instrument is better than with iron, and they said this due to the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they claimed that the wound from cautery does not cause infection, but this is not true as I have proven it, and found that it indeed happens in some people; and cauterization with gold is better than with iron, just as they stated.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a golden instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of gold, and it cools down so quickly; and if one heats it too much, they burn themselves on fire; thus there are enough obstacles to this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cautery which we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter from head to foot so that the material is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for moisture and coldness in the brain, and it is applied due to two reasons: because of a disease called 'soda', and because of the excess humours which descend from the head into the eyes, ears, causing numerous dreams, toothache, sore throat, and all diseases stemming from cold such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged by medicine three or four nights in a row, according to their health and tolerance for purgatives; then have them fast on the fifth night.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, 
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on an ink-stained surface, and move your hand in a downward and squeezing motion repeatedly while twisting; then lift your hand slightly, and reexamine the area if you see the bone protruding even slightly; if you don't see it, repeat the cauterization process until you do see the bone as I instructed you; afterward take some softened wax, and place moistened cotton within it, and put it on the site; leave it there for three days; then apply butter-soaked cotton; keep it in place until the scalding has subsided; finally treat the wound with a healing ointment known as "tetrafarmacum" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients say that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges itself; thus aiding healing.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one must let the cautery burn until a part of the bone is charred, then remove what has been burnt from the bone and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one must let the cautery remain in place, pressing down so hard that it pierces the bone like a needle that women use in their sewing, allowing the humors to escape; and they should leave the wound open for some time before cleaning and suturing it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	These two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me at all, except in certain individuals where there is fear; and I believe it should be left up to the doctor as each case may vary depending on the condition of the patient's body; for the bone has been weakened by continuous natural processes, just like we see in other limbs; even if the patient's bone is weak by nature, and the first method seems safer and more useful to me, thus I use it when I practice medicine.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the entire head is afflicted with chronic pain that persists for a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, as well as oils and plasters; if one performs on them the cauterisation we previously mentioned, it will be of no avail.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take heed if the patient's shoulder is of a strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterise it below that cautery we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards, perform the cauterisation on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we previously stated, and also cauterise it in the place called "vasselz"; these are the places where cups for cupping therapy are placed; be gentle with your hand so that you do not reach the bone: the patient will feel much greater pain in this cauterisation than in the others, but I shall speak of that later; and make sure that the cauteries on the corners are more subtle than those used to cauterise the middle part of the head, and here is how:
dou cautere dou chief	For the cauterization of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head and extends to the eye, and the scalp is cleansed with softening medicines, and other treatments I mentioned in the section on diseases have been applied, but none are effective: then you should use cauterization in two ways, that is, with hot iron and medicine.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with medicine is done as follows: take a piece of alder wood, remove the bark and cut it into two pieces, then make an incision in the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the alder wood underneath the skin; when it is placed, bind and hold it firmly for twelve hours; then release and treat with strong garlic, leaving the wound open for two or three days; afterward, apply cotton soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment, let it heal completely; and if you wish to do so, use some of the burning medications that I have written about in the twelfth chapter on burning medications.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with which you have this shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called a "key" because its head is made in the shape of a key with a slight curvature, and in the middle there is a small protuberance; place it on the painful area, and hold your hand while slightly turning the iron so that half of the heart-shaped edge is scorched; lift your hand so as not to burn the artery, which lies above it, from where a lot of blood will flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in the eye of silk, and put it over for III days; then apply moist cotton with butter, and then treat the area of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine using the cautery called "cultellare", take care not to cut the artery during this ancient practice.
de emigraine	Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have previously mentioned in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cauteries described before by medicine or iron do not suffice, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; mark a line with half a finger's length on the spot, withdraw your hand once, and be careful not to cut the artery nor reach the bone; beware of affecting the mandible that moves when we chew food, or else spasms may arise in the patient, and take care against profuse bleeding from the artery if it is severed, which carries great peril especially for those who are inexperienced and unpracticed; leave the work halfway. I will tell you how to staunch blood flow when an artery is cut, and I shall show you where this is described in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is still suffering, cauterize him on his head as we have said before, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you observe this, administer the cautery which we mentioned in the chapter about arterial extraction, with the double-bladed cautery; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of ear pain due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When ear pain arises from the cold, and you have applied softening medicines and other treatments as we mentioned before, but the pain persists, heat up this cautery called a "pin," which is shaped like this:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both ears, and move away a little above the root of the ear from where you have marked the spot for cauterization; and make ten pin-pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	From the mouth's torment.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated by cauterization is limited to those caused by flux, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not apply cautery to similar conditions arising from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this similar condition of torture caused by flux from ulcers and purging of the head, as well as gargling, and it does not improve, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third where the two lips meet; place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and apply the cautery towards the head, just above the ear's tip, and another on the temple about as long as a thumb; leave the cauterization until half of the heart has been burned; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is similar to the instrument we described before, but it is slightly more subtle, and the blade should be a little thicker; after treating the site as I mentioned earlier, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have described, but there is no improvement, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the location called "vessels" as mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; they should be treated as described earlier.
de litargie	Of lethargy:
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that purify the brain; afterwards wash his head thoroughly, and apply to the occiput a sinapi cataplasm which is described in the treatise on cataplasms; and this is how you perform the cautery: do as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, apply three fire cauterizations from the middle of the head down to the neck, leaving a two-finger space between each one; treat them like the others, and if you see fit to adjust it, and the patient can tolerate it, apply one cautery in the center; and if necessary, apply two more on the two corners, treating until it is healed; and let these cauterizations be called 'olive-like', as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	Of the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed of hairs and according to what we have said before; after, grasp the patient's head, then apply a cautery in the middle of the head and on each corner, and one behind, and three along the spine of the neck; if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, apply four cauterizations along the spine of the back; let them burn until the greatest part of the heart is burnt, then lift your hand; treat until it is healed, and let these cauterizations be called 'olive-like' as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cautery unless they are phlegmatic; one must first modify the brain with herbs and other treatments as we have mentioned in previous chapters when the patient is large and suffers from difficulty taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, perform gargling and chewing often with herbs to modify the brain; after, raise their head in the middle [of the room], and perform a cauterisation as we have mentioned before on the crown of the head, and cauterise each corner; and if the patient is strong and suffers, perform cautery as I said for one who has paralysis and softening of the body, along the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-sized according to the manner I have mentioned.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform this subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause of melancholy is due to excess or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize with multiple cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause of melancholy is due to excess declining into melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink so that the brain may be cleansed, as was said before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, wipe the patient's head; then make a well-formed linen pad, like a ring, and place it in the middle of the head; have the patient sit with crossed legs, and hold them steady from all sides; apply the liniment, which is preferably old sheep butter; heat it to a warm temperature so that the skin can tolerate it when applied; after emptying the circle inside the head, let it cool down; do this once a week for the patient along with other good treatments until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you are cauterizing with fire, make multiple punctures all over the cautery site.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of fire cautery softens the brain considerably; then apply moistened cotton with butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	The eyelid.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the swelling first appears on the eyelids through signs I mentioned before in this section, then start and give the patient something purifying for the head, protect him from all moisture, and make him sweat with multiple baths while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, instruct him to lower his head and cauterize between the temples with two cauteries if the swelling descends into both eyes together or one if it is in only one; make sure you avoid all veins and arteries located under the heart and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; beware of blood loss, and should you see too much blood coming out, then stop the bleeding as far as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will instruct you in the extraction of arteries and the incision, cautioning how to stem it; sometimes one makes a cautery or hot iron below the two rear bones.
dou cors des larmes	The body's tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to being on the veins, or near the arteries that appear outside the head; and one sees that they are cold, phlegmatic excesses, then apply the cautery as I said at the beginning, descending towards the eyes: one cauterization in the middle of the head, two cauterizations above the temples, and two cauterizations with a hot iron below the two rear bones; if more is needed, cautiously cauterize just above the eyebrows using small cauterizations.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Through the body of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit from it, then give the patient to drink three nights with cock's grease; afterwards, raise his head, and cauterize him in the middle of the olive [bone]; and make two cauterizations of the "clavicle" cautery above the two wrists, a little below the hairline; and be wary of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the "clavicle" cautery:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the papilla of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that do two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyelashes are; and do not leave your hand there unless until a third part of the paper is burnt, according to the manner I said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes turn inward, and prick the eye, so one makes cauterizations according to two methods: namely with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards draw on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put moist cotton with egg white and parsley poultice on the eye, then heat up the cautery for which this is the shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize on the figure that you have marked little by little many times, until the heart of the area is burnt; and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the paper retracting, and the hairs rise to the level of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then put moist cotton in butter until the scald is gone; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs grow and the skin softens again, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did before; but if the hair has fallen out, cauterize until the skin is raised to its natural level, and is even, without pricking the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cauteries of medicine are what you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow large and evenly, then make parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; do this quickly so it does not cool, then spread it on the form you made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin around the eyes; if the disease is in only one eye, operate on that one, but if both are affected as well; place underneath the eye cotton moistened with egg white; the patient's head should be in your lap and put your finger pointing toward the medicine, press his chest and move the eyeball whenever the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine because he will feel it like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the wound has healed, lift up the place of water, and observe if you see the skin raised just as it was raised by the effect of fire or due to an incision; and if this is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, apply medicine again to the place where it has opened, until your treatments are even and your eyes focused; then put moist cotton soaked in butter until the burnt flesh is removed, after heal the place of ointment which is called 'diaphenis' or another, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must, be very careful with your work to ensure that none of the medicine reaches the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft later on, and hairs grow in the eye, repeat the medicine on that spot where the paper has softened properly, just as you did before; after healing it so it is cured; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your restrictions; and do not abandon the right path for one who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	on the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head on your hand; hold their head with both hands firmly so it cannot move or twist; then apply moistened cotton soaked in egg white or parsley juice onto the eye; afterwards heat this cautery, which is shaped like a vaulted feather, combined together as one piece; if you wish, point it from one end to another, and if you wish, make it tent-shaped; but nevertheless, this vaulted shape is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards press the fistula if it is open, and remove any pus, then dry it; but if it is closed, operate on it, and push outwards from the brow; afterwards place a hot cautery like this nearby, hold your hand over the cautery at the part above the nail towards the eye, so your hand does not move; apply the cautery to the fatty tissue of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you go all the way to the bone with the cauterization, it would be beneficial.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, repeat the cauterization again and use as much as needed, leaving it for three days; afterwards, apply moist cotton wool soaked in butter, and treat with a drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass without healing, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat according to what comes up in this chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a type of cauterization for fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	For fistula, cut into the site, then insert in the incision one fine catgut of such quality as to fit its shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	et they make it to the quantity of one .З. of lead; and hold your hand or hammer firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the molten lead does not run into his eye; and you must place on the patient's eye moist cotton soaked in egg white or water: the lead thus fills the place of the fistula, and heals with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, you must administer an aperture with a knife, and return the fistula to the body of the knife according to what is necessary in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times, cracks occur on lips which are called "chaps," especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as mentioned before in various ways, and the treatment is ineffective, then heat a small knifepoint cautery according to this method:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the cracks until it reaches the bottom; then treat the area with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	for an abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the tonsil, or in the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes pain and becomes swollen; it turns into a fistula and is treated as mentioned before, but if this treatment does not work, then you must use a cautery according to the size of the fistula. Then open the fistula's pore, hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom or back, do this once or twice; afterwards treat it like we said in treatments until it is healed. If it heals well, great! If not, then you must uncover the area and remove any rotten bone as per what you find specified in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	By the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't work, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterward, heat the cauterization tool that will be described below in such a way that you put a cane over the tooth; and insert the hot cautery inside quickly, holding your hand so the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your desire; afterward, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water, and hold it for an hour then rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth becomes confirmed in place, and the softened gum restrained, with the moisture corrupting it drying up.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises due to coldness, whether it is cold or hot, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cauterization is necessary according to two methods: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is performed as follows: take cow's butter and place a small amount in an iron or brass spoon; then wrap cotton around the tip of a stick and dip it into the melted butter, applying it to the aching tooth until it cools down; repeat this frequently so that its properties reach the root of the tooth. To do this, you can also soak wool and cotton in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth while placing hot iron on top until heat reaches the base of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cauterizations with fire are such that you should take a cane of iron or copper, and make it thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterward heat the cauterization tool, from which its form will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cauterization is cooled; do this often, because the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the urgency of the cauterization, and then cool it off afterward; and this is the form of the cauterization tool:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cauterization tool for any part of the head that you wish, and according to your ability; and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	Some scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofula is of phlegm and cold moisture, and does not obey digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery with a chimney from which smoke comes out afterwards through two openings in the other part; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or as many times as necessary until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small put the cautery according to the size of the abscess and leave it for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter until the burn is removed; afterwards treat the area with ointments and dressings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The chimney's shape:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overwhelms the channels of the lung, especially when it originates from cold constitution, then the patient should be cleansed first with dissolving medicines; afterwards perform cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to reach the throat, and burn no more than a small portion of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards perform another cautery at the joint where the neck meets the skull along the spine, and let the cauterization be of the type called 'clavile' as described before; treat the site as mentioned earlier until it is healed.
de la toust	Of coughing.
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all lung ailments are caused by cold moisture, and the patient lacks fever or dryness, especially with an old illness, perform two cauterizations over the muscles in the armpits; another one between the breasts closer to the chest; and let these cauterizations be of the type called 'clavile' according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform the fire cautery by puncturing throughout all of the cauterization points called 'points' which are formed as such in ear diseases; and let these points be up to thirty, or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the location according to what has been previously stated, let the cauterization be in three rows following this pattern:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauterizations are lighter, for you will do three at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the ribs, and the shape of the cautery would comprise four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with three irons, thus forming six cauterizations; and these nerves are arranged according to a subtle pattern, and this is the form of the cautery with three irons.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	and sometimes it is arranged above this single nerve, for which there would be eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then place the cautery on top, crush the bell with oil; afterwards make the patient rest and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well fortified.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, then something happens quickly; therefore make a clavicle cautery on the thick part or apply many small cauteries by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joints are closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When cold and excessive moisture enter the stomach to such an extent that it disrupts their natural balance, and catarrh increases within them, and customary treatments do not provide relief, then the patient must be reminded to sit upright on their back, extending their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Thereafter you should perform three cautery treatments underneath the armpit with a tablespoon size for each treatment, and two cautery procedures outside both sides of the chest to form a triangle shape, leaving enough space between them so that they do not join together when pouring out pus; and ensure the cauterization is thorough, reaching both parts of the heart, and make the cautery figure according to this form without adjustment: [diagram].
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	Et si tu veux cautériser avec un grand cautère dans l'estomac selon cette forme ; et celui qui aura peur de ce cautère, cautérise en piquant et saignant sur l'estomac à ce point selon la quantité que tu veux prendre ensuite ; cautérise le tout avec le cautère appelé « poinçonnement ».
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Après le traitement du traitement que nous avons eu précédemment, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver is in pain due to cold and moisture and has a large gaseous distension, it has been thrown out of its natural balance by excesses ; and the patient is treated as we have said previously, but it does not benefit him, so the patient must be reminded of his condition; apply three cauterizations according to this form and figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the man's coat comes from ; and leave a space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger ; and let the cauteries be as long as the body, and do not press your hand too much throughout the cautery ; and only burn half of the heart, and have the patient standing upright on his feet ; and if he cannot stand, then let him lie down, and stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms ; and this is the form :
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your intention is to cauterize these knife cautery marks, then do so carefully if you are skilled and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the entire heart, as it would dry out the whole body; and don't go near the mouth, for the heart is very delicate there, and know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel pain but not too intense; if it is in the membrane, they will experience excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And so, when this treatment is required, the patient must be reminded to keep their head still; then lance the site where the abscess is located, and afterward cauterize with a tool similar in shape to a ray, which will form like this:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the fire cautery until the heart is burnt, and it reaches as far as the syphac, so that the pores are all closed; afterwards treat it according to the cure for boils until it is healed; and no one should use this cautery other than a doctor who has studied medicine long enough, by whose hands some of these illnesses have been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may operate boldly, yet it seems to me that one would be better letting him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Wax cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for wax cautery one should make cauteries from the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a root of aristolochia, long, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, also as thick and as long as your two fingers; soak it in oil, then put it to fire, and cauterize with the cautery between the armpit and the neck, and two small cauteries a little downwards on the part that is below the beard; two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, sloping backwards a little; one cautery in the middle of the breast, another above the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on either side of the breast outside the cautery that is between the two shoulders; do not press your hand hard, but apply it gently as if perfuming.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient scholars said that men should use a cauterizing fire similar to a barber's razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches this abscess; and if it causes pain, as we have mentioned in the case of liver abscesses.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have said in the section on treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three types of cauterization, all of which are beneficial.
