You must therefore, when this occurs in any man, look to see if the wound is fresh and full of blood; then join the two lips together with a suture, and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already torn apart on one side or the other, you must scrape away all the parts of their heart until they bleed, then bring the two lips together with a suture, hold them in place, and sprinkle over them dragon's blood powder and powdered incense; put on top of the powders a piece of strong emplastron or other soldering emplastron, and leave it until it sticks by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of suturing is such that you bring together the edges: either with needles, as we have said for stitching the abdomen; or with thread, as I made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	Ulcers of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Skilled surgeons find within the lips a hard abscess, similar to wheat grains, smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn back the lips, cut open each nodule, grasp it with pincers, and cut it into pieces in every part; afterwards fill the place after incision with ground vitriol until the blood is dried up; and then leave it alone, treating the area with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	On the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; 
des sordens	Of abscesses
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	None are ever joined to the head of the teeth within the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green as the decay reaches the gum, and they stink; so you must seat the patient with their head in your lap, and shave off all the scabs until nothing remains; do the same for the blackness and greenness, yellowness, and other faults so that they are clean; if you remove what is there due to the first cause it will be good; otherwise start again on the second day and third until you have removed everything; know that teeth need various forms of instrument to scrape, according as work demonstrates, for the scraper used outside the teeth has a different shape from those which are used between them; all these shapes should be at hand.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay in extracting it as much as you can, because one must not do this; for it is a very delicate substance until such time as one has no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract it, you must be certain of which tooth is causing pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and they think it is in a healthy tooth, so they extract the good one; however, the pain remains because of this, as the bad tooth still remains, for we have already seen this with other patients; and when you are certain which tooth is causing pain, you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gums on all sides; then move your fingers or delicate pliers into its first hole and hole, until it is well loosened, then firmly close the pliers; and let the patient's head be in your lap between your knees, hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it cannot be done, take one of these instruments and gently insert it on each side, moving it just like you did previously.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the hole is; then gently grasp it with pincers, taking care not to break it while extracting it; one must work very carefully around the gum in order to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break it and leave a piece behind, as the remaining root can cause even greater pain for the patient later on.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware of not doing what the ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and boldness sometimes break the jawbone, and fail to manage what we have described; but instead bring about serious diseases due to the roots remaining or the jaw being broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is removed, wash the place with wine or oil and silk; if there is bleeding, which often occurs, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one pulls out teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick bodies so that they do not bend when pulling, and be well-made iron, and toothed in order to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, it is necessary that you place moist cotton soaked in butter over the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the spot softens, you can insert the tongs which are called "algefri", making the head look like a stork's beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument known as 'althali', that is to say, a probe, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be thick and strong so as not to break, and if the root comes out with it, that is good; but if not, you must assist with all of the instruments, which are shown hereafter in their respective forms.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one needs assistance with this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other iron instruments that are used in the region of the teeth, as well as this instrument resembling large pincers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Et soit cist estrumens fors qu'il ne puisse brisier, 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And [the head] should be thick and hold well to keep the bone in place, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; then restore its position with appropriate medicine, and if there is any decay in the bone, and it is small, take it away with all these instruments.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form and they are ugly, especially in virgin women, then you must know if the tooth is newly born after another one, and it is not in its right place, nor can be filed or smoothed; therefore, extract it; and if it has air with the other teeth, take this instrument described here, which resembles a small beak, and let it be made of iron, sharp at the top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And strike it often with a hammer while in open air for the hardness of the tooth, and so you do not move others, and if it is apparent that one can file [the tooth], then smoothen it with such a file as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file of which needles are made; and with a file one wears down teeth point by point over many days slightly, so that they do not move until they fall out; then completely at the end for any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and wounds the tongue, it is necessary to file its harshness until it is even, so that it does not wound the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When front teeth loosen due to impact or falling and the patient cannot chew without them dropping out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, which is ineffective; then they must be restrained by a gold wire, for silver wires turn green and decay but gold never changes; and let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the wire and pass it doubled between two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth or teeth between them until you arrive safely at a sound tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering until reaching the part where you began, and gently extract your hand carefully so that there is no movement; and make the tie at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the shoulder's head with a thread using pliers, and assemble them, and reattach it between the healthy teeth, putting it in place so that it does not injure the tongue; then leave it tight as much as it can stay like this, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread; thus it will remain and serve for its entire time, and here is the model of teeth and the image of the alignment of two healthy teeth and two displaced ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, fresh for fresh, as we have said; and do not let anyone who is not wise and patient intervene, and sometimes a tooth model made of cow bone is used, placing it where there is a lack, and they are tightened like we've mentioned before, remaining thus serving for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue's tie
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	For this kind of tongue-tie is natural and present from birth, or it may result from an injury that has healed; the procedure for such a condition requires you to open the mouth of the patient with their head in your lap, then lift the tongue and cut the nerve tie, ensuring the tongue is released from its enclosure. If there is any scar tissue or swelling due to sudden injury, insert a hook and cut across this bond broadly. Be careful not to cut too deeply through the incision for fear of damaging the artery beneath; once complete, rinse with rosewater and oil, or cold water only, then place a linen tent under the tongue as protection from the wound. The patient should keep their mouth open each night so that the wounds do not heal over quickly.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply crushed vitriol to the spot; and should the blood beat strongly, cauterize it with the lenticular cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you see it change color to white or black or become hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancerous ulcer; and if it begins to turn pale and moist, cut away the edges with an uncine, and open it with a fine spatule, and remove it from both sides; and if the blood beats strongly towards your work, apply crushed vitriol until it subsides, then return to your work until everything is treated; then lift the wound with lint and silk, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes boils appear inside the throat called 'godath', properly known as the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in our classification, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess with little sensation and false colour, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron, also due to the loss of blood; but leave it until it ripens, and then you will remove it, or it will rupture on its own; and if it is white in colour, soft, and the root is subtle, prepare your instrument for cutting, but first ensure the abscess has cooled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all these instruments, and you see the abscess, take the hook and insert it into the almond, then pull upward as hard as you can; draw out anything from the cloth along with it, then cut around the instrument which looks like a forceps; however, the tip is curved, and one part meets another, they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument available, use the pincers which look like it:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And they are sharp on one side and blunt on the other; when you have cut into one of the almonds, do so with the other in the same manner, then after incising gargle the patient's throat with warm water mixed with salt, and with water and vinegar if there is bleeding; use only water to gargle if there is no bleeding but a discharge of blood. Use peels from pomegranates boiled in water, or leaves of myrtle tree, and similar things until all bleeding has stopped; then treat until it heals; sometimes other abscesses form besides the two almonds, so cut these as you would the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had formed inside her throat; it was small, but almost completely blocked her airway so that she could not breathe through it, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if left like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess had risen so high that two tubes had been inserted through the nostrils to help her breathe.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore hastened to act and inserted a tube into one nostril, then pushed it upwards, and a large piece of bowels came out with it; then I repeated the process in the other nostril, opening her mouth and pressing on her tongue; after that, I inserted the tube into the abscess and cut away a part of it, only a little blood came out; thus the airway was cleared and the woman could now drink water and later wine, and I did not stop cutting away at this abscess for a long time; but then it grew back again, filling up the space that I had emptied until it became very large; so I swallowed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts, trusting God to take care of her from there on.
de l’uve	Of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the grape descends [into the mouth] and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called a "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cleaned as we have said in the division, and the cleaning does not benefit [the patient], and you see that the surrounding abscesses are relieved, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is round gathered together and not long; and it is bloody or false coloured or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have described, regarding its whiteness and length, that you seat the patient in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument which we have previously mentioned; then insert the lancet into the grape, and draw it out, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned for the incision of the testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut away any flesh beyond what is superfluous and outside the natural limit; for if you remove more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two almonds (tonsils), and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then you must employ an engine for cauterization to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is quicksilver (mercury).
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	The patient should place their head in your lap and then press their tongue to the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery. Confine it with hot quicksilver, neither too thick nor too thin, using this tool whose shape is thus:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this way, take calmly and assemble hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and mugwort and similar herbs, and put them all together or some of them into one pot, add vinegar, and boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have a perforated instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it [the perforated instrument] should be made of silver or copper, and one end of the instrument is placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises up to their throat until the throat tissue dies; afterwards, repeat this often, until the tissue dries out, and make sure you do not perform this procedure at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many complications can arise; nor should it be done except when the hot abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth so their mouth does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not allow vapors to harm the mouth, and it is a good treatment along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times an object gets stuck in the throat - a fish bone or something else; therefore, you must extract what is visible and press the tongue with your tool to see the object move. For what cannot be seen and remains lodged in the throat, make the patient vomit before food is digested so that perhaps the object comes up by vomiting; or let them swallow a piece of sponge, or a bit of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry bread crumb; tie a thread to the sponge then let it be swallowed. When it reaches its place, it will swell and then pull out with forceps. If not successful using these methods take this tool shaped as follows:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be bent towards the head so that they can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head raised upwards; and make sure you do not touch the epiglottis, otherwise it will swell up, and do not push against the bone with force; and it is better if the patient pushes the instrument in themselves, as they are aware of where things are located inside them; thus either let him insert it downwards or pull it towards himself with all his might until he feels resistance.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the blood of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never should blood be used as medicine, as I said in the division regarding medical treatment; and if this does not bring benefit, then look into the patient's throat towards the sun, while pressing their tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, draw it out with a small hook or delicate forceps suited to this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a tuft of hair and push it into the patient's throat, then insert the other end of the hair into a hot iron, doing this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is afflicted with water-drinking every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water and open the patient's mouth, pouring it in without swallowing, moving their hand often; as soon as the leech senses the water, it will fall off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then suffumigate the patient with asafoetida, using an instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this several times, for it will fall without harming them.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et the manner of the fumigation is that you take a pot with visible coals, and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, and place the instrument's head into this opening; then add your fumigant, and have the patient put the end of the pipe into their mouth, closing their mouth so no smoke escapes but reaches down to the lungs; and now the mucus will come out, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation several times; let the sick person suffer thirst, eating salty things only, drinking no water; then the phlegm shall be expelled by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats phlegm, when it can be seen, is like bent tongs to insert into the throat; and it has a resemblance to a bird's beak, and has the roughness of a file, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go; and here is its form: [Insert diagram or image as appropriate]
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what is remembered and written about in this book, and they vary in their perforation and size; and there are two main kinds, one based on their appearance itself, and the other depending on the moisture it holds.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is determined by where they appear in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and abscesses in fleshy places differ from those that appear in joints, and each requires its own specific treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And one should not incise an abscess unless the boil is fully ripe according to its development; and for those that require incision when they are hard, but do not ripen fully, as with abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses appear near joints, and it is left untreated with the surrounding flesh being rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contractions in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforating it until it dies, it will harm the principal member; when it's near the foundation, pierce it before it dies; do not pierce an abscess formed without complete digestion, except for one near the foundation, which can rot thoroughly, elongate inside, become a fistula, and won't heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	You must know the opening of the abscess's perforation that is dead according to its development, which happens when pain eases, fever lessens, soreness and redness diminish, swelling subsides, and other signs; ensure the incision sits under the lowest part of the abscess, where it moves; make the perforation as long as the body part, and if the abscess is on hands or feet, joints, nerves, or arteries, make incisions in all equal places without folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in fleshy tissue, it is better that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed as digested fully, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that, the body of the abscess would be elongated and filled with much filth, and by chance the lips and depth of its cavity may have hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And for any abscess that is punctured according to the width of its body, let it be treated according to the needs of the affected limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must apply small incisions for small abscesses, and large incisions for large abscesses, making multiple slits according to the size of the abscess, and if there are such abscesses that require removal of their core, and excision; when it becomes like linen cloth, and is softened, one should treat them as boils: And if there are some which split into three angles, and others like those incised like a myrtle leaf, like abscesses from carbuncles; and there are those where we make round cuts, other kinds of incision and excision.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits jump sometimes with the discharge of bile, which may cause the patient's death, and you will not perceive it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Remove this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound dry, and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it's a full-blown sore, apply strips of linen or old cotton; and for large abscesses with many perforations, place a strip in each hole so that they touch one another; and if you've peeled back part of the skin over the abscess, filling it up with dry cotton wool or pieces of old linen cloth without moisture, bind it up until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, bring cold and light water, wet some cloths, and place them over the bleeding site repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply warm compresses and healing ointment, and use the powders I mentioned in various places throughout this book. If it is winter and the skin or abscess is very sensitive, you should put on tents and cloths moistened with warm wine and oil; but if it is summertime and the flesh is fleshy, use cloths dampened with water and oil, or cold wine and oil, for up to three days, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wipe it clean, and treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed with treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the head of the skull comes small abscesses arise, and they are like veils, just as the yolk of an egg, and there is much that resembles them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and soft where there is moisture like pulses; and there are some which are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the artery does not act contrary (to this).
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting into it is such that you test every instrument which is called an 'entromissoire', from whence its form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if moisture is present, they do it above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, carefully scrape away anything leaving behind the skin containing this moisture, for it returns if nothing is left there; then apply Egyptian ointment with cotton, if present; if not, use water and salt, place it on the wound, and leave it until the next day; those remaining from the night will be driven out.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then repeat the cotton application as before on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for healing, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains fatty material, then cut it open in this manner, from the long side; and remove pus, and scrape away tissue from all sides, and put all your effort into milking out the contents where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you previously.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also of the abscess if it is fistulous, and of cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the fistulous abscess and the moist area is lighter, for they have little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in some of these abscesses or heads where there is no moisture, and like the abscess I cut from the head of an old woman; I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck any of them, they would have also made a wound as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming to the head, like those that come to children's heads and at the roots of ears, the opening should always be in the lowest place, so the pus can flow out; and treat them as required.
des scrophules	The lumps of swelling
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck and beneath the armpits, in the groin, sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, tangled together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each swelling is properly within its own boundary, like the knot and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar types of these swellings.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones which do not obey healthy practices.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those which you see of good disposition to touch, and are similar in color to the body, and move from each part without being close to the nerves of the neck nor the artery or tube, and is not deep; you must cut it from above, and peel off its skin on all sides, and extend the two lips of the heart with tweezers if necessary, as we have said for abscesses of the head; then withdraw slowly, being sure that you do not cut any nerve nor vein, and be careful not to use a sharp or pointed tool lest your hand slip, and do not go too deep so as to avoid cutting what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then apply crushed vitriol or some powders that staunch blood into the wound, and bind the wound; leave it until the abscess is pacified, and the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Once the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then check with your right index finger if there are any small scrofulae remaining, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large wound in the root of the scrofula, you should not cut this scrofula at its root but bind it with a strong double thread and let it fall by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire scrofula, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and suture them now, since there is no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must proceed to cut the root of it, extract any pus, and suture as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For scrofulas with excess flesh, puncture where it seems dead and remove this as described above, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things so that they draw out the corruption; and when the wound is clean, treat it with healing ointments until it heals.
de squinance	For scabies.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke of the throat surgery; but I never saw one performed in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	Those who have difficulty should ensure that the slit in the throat, known as the epiglottis, is clear; and one must not provide aid for them, because all the veins and passages of the patient are affected by those with an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the passage of the airway, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to slit the epiglottis, we must make an incision beneath three circles or four in a small crosswise slit between two circles or by the quantity of the upper slit, not into the cartilage; and these are suitable for the sectioning of the epiglottis as there is no flesh here, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he must extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then split the heart until it reaches the windpipe; remove the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syphon, as we have said; it is proven by the section of the windpipe that [the heart] should be there where it is broken, and by the defect of the voice; leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the time has passed that we fear strangulation, join the two lips of the heart's wound, and sew them together without the cartilage; then administer medicine that grows flesh until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely blocked and the patient is judged to be dying, with no breath left.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, thus keeping him safe from death; and for this reason, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the poison of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they ordered the wound to be sewn and treated, so that it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took one knife and stuck it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, knowing well that she had not cut her vein or damaged her lungs, and air was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, treating it until it was healed; there only remained for the young lady to recover her voice, after which she would return to normal, I say this so that in tailoring the epiglottis one need not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a large one with a yellow color, more common in women; and it happens in two ways: natural, or accidental; wherein there is no engyn.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type happens in two ways similar to what we call 'fat' and abscess caused by arterial damage; where there is fear, it should not be opened with fire unless if small, first test and investigate thoroughly: whether you find it as our fat without veins, then cut like a nail, pulling out its root completely if present, acting quickly, treating as necessary until fully healed.
des nous	Des nous
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You must, when you come to treat the eye, first test and examine all the instrument called an 'introducer', according to its form as it will appear in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses in newborns is that you take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth until you know the instrument has pierced the core, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, taking care not to lose it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is short and whatever its colour, do to it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the introducer no moisture comes out, know that it is greasy, so make a cross incision and take it with pincers, flaying it lightly on either side and preserve the coat where it lies so you draw it healthy with the eye; and if you cannot draw it whole and healthy, then do so by pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the wound will return many times; and if even a little stays put and blood flows out of it, fill up the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, secure it tight, apply warm dressings to suppress abscesses, treat it with other remedies until it heals entirely; but should the wound be large, cut open both lips of the wound, then heal them as flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the fresh wound is contrary to you or otherwise prevents haste then apply crushed vitriol, and leave it there for two or three days until the wound suppurates and stops the blood's boiling; return again to remove whatever remains of the nightshade.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Observe here the shapes of instruments used in incisions and they are three kinds: large, medium and small; also four called "albaret" and one called a "beeb", these too come in three sizes: large, medium and small to encircle abscesses or fistula; there are also needles for cutting sutures made from brass, iron or silver, the yellow ones being preferable with black lead preferred for encisting fistulas; again they come in three sizes according to the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of uncines are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are uncines with two curves in three different ways; and there are uncines with three curves, also in three different ways; and there are uncines with two curves, and uncines with a single curve only, again in three different ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these are made sharp, and there are some that only cut on one side, which helps to avoid damaging nerves or veins when excising; and of these introducers, there are several types of dilators, so the patient does not feel it during the opening of abscesses; and they come in three different sizes: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one only uses them on fleshy parts such as legs, arms, breasts, or similar areas; and sometimes a smaller instrument is made, resembling scalpels, according to this form, which helps stop bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed back into position to heal by closing the veins and arteries, and sometimes this follows this great shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, making them appear like female breasts; they remain ugly and swollen, and for those who wish to cure it, one must follow this shape from point b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat and fill the wound with meat-promoting medicine, then join the two lips of the wound together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; if the breast hangs downwards and is softened due to its size as happens in women, make an incision through it into two parts by means of two similar cuts so that one part supports the other at the end of each, such that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from line b up to g; then scrape away the skin which lies between the two lips and remove the fat, apply what we have said about sutures and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure until it is healed; if it isn't healed or the incision has not been completed due either to the patient's unwillingness to rest or to blood loss, you must fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; leave it there until all the remaining flesh and fat have been consumed then treat it until it is completely healed.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come beneath the armpits are like hard scrofula with sides, and there is moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the matter within the abscess is emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like a scrofula, cut it as we have said for cutting scrofulas, and if the wound yields matter, apply cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of an artery rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When an artery is ruptured, and the skin above it has sealed, many abscesses often form, and similarly, swelling occurs in the vein along with abscesses; you can identify this when it is due to the artery as the abscess runs longitudinally throughout; and when you feel it with your fingers, there is a constriction felt; and if it's due to the vein, it appears swollen outwardly; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it lies below the elbows, armpits, neck, and many other places, as it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid iron treatment, and also for the head wound, it must be avoided, especially in cases of arterial swelling that penetrates through the skin; then make an incision with a lancet, carefully separating the artery from its surrounding tissues until it is exposed; next, insert a needle beneath it, piercing it all the way to the other side, and tie off the artery with double thread at two points as I've shown you for the temple arteries; then puncture the place between the two ties with an introducer until blood flows out of it, and release the abscess; then provide treatment that involves gentle stretching until the threads fall away; cure the wound by applying appropriate ointments until it is healed; if the abscess results from incising a vein, one must grasp as much of the abscess and skin together as possible with their hand, insert a needle underneath where they hold it in their hand, pierce through it, and thread double thread there so that you draw them out on the other side; then bind up the abscess by tying threads between two places at either end, as I've explained to you; if you doubt whether the threads will pull through, insert another needle with a single thread beneath all of the abscess to the first incision point and tie these together in four places; next, open the abscess so that its excess material is released, cut away the redundant part of the heart and leave behind what's bound up; then apply a cloth moistened with wine and oil, provide treatment using tents and ointments until it has healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also abscesses occur in the artery and in the vein, abscesses arise on nerves when they are damaged or through excessive work, and similar cases.
