Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And these occur more frequently on shoulders and fingers and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it appears in various locations without pain; and when one presses firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not located within the flesh but beneath the heart; and it spreads in every direction, neither forward nor backward, nor below nor above, and an abscess on a joint should not be cut with an iron instrument: perhaps contraction would occur; and if it is on the head or forehead, apply balsam.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with forceps and cut it at its root; if it is large, suspend it with a hook, then peel and remove it, stitch up the wound, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes they occur on the belly and nowhere else in the body, it is a disease called "fungus" due to its resemblance to fungi, with a subtle root and large head; there are small and very large ones; I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like mushrooms than anything else, with no difference between them, they were white, had fine roots, were light brown split open, and moisture was coming out.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six З., and for the operation of incising it is that you watch if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist from a subtle root; so cut it with a broad spatule, and have cauterization by fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when cutting it often leads to great loss of blood, and if the blood beats you, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient scared and fearful of the incision with iron, then take a well-made thread of lead, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, do not cease from binding the thread of lead until you cut the artery, and each by itself without work; and if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut especially in the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and take care not to cut the vein which is a pale color and poor sense of milk aspect.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enhanced, and I will come to the treatment of cancer afterward.
quant li boude ist fuer	When it is swollen with pus.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the abscess arises from cauterizing wounds or cracks in boils, and it is on the belly with some swelling, just as happens in other sores, or from blood that comes out of veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from gas; and if it is due to the rupture of a boil and the emission of pus, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, being a slight thing without pain, appearing with different discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is more varied: when you press it with your fingers and it protrudes, and then returns back inwards; sometimes it appears to be constricted, growing greatly at the entrance of the bath and during hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor issue, and you can tell this by how easily it moves when pressed with your hand, as it offers no resistance; but if it is due to blood, then these signs will appear - large, hard abscesses that are fixed in one place according to their quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and you must consider whether this appearance is due to arterial or venous blood, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You should leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is of the intestine or rectum, you should instruct the patient to hold their breath and lie flat on their back; then bleed them all around the belly; then have them lay frequently in your hands, then go around the place that you marked with a span's length; then stretch half of the abscess above the large inch; then bind it tightly with a strong thread or thick silk cord, so that the knot is below; then operate on the stretched part of the abscess that lies above the knot and insert your index finger, seeking out the intestine; if you find it caught by the knot, then untie it and push the intestine outside the abdomen; and if you find the rectum, grasp it with the inch, cutting away any excess; and if an artery or vein obstructs you, carefully go around it, then return to your task and take two needles, insert two lengths of strong thread through them, and insert the two needles into what you have previously pierced in a cross pattern; then drain the abscess by stretching it open over four points along the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles and leave the place alone until it rots, and cut away the dead flesh as it becomes soft and rotten; then treat the area according to your judgement, and close the abscess as we have said; then drain out any blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place with what is required, and seal the wound.
dou chancre	From cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have spoken about the appearances of cancer and how it should be treated with medicine, and how to avoid surgical treatment. We mention cancer arising in the marrow and the great caution needed for its cure; the ancients say that when cancer is located where it can be scraped away like cancers of the breast, thigh, and similar places, it must all be removed at the outset; but when they are large and ancient, you should not approach them because I have never been able to cure any such case nor has anyone else ever done so before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is located where it can be removed as we have said, involves purging the patient once with black bile; then making them bleed if there is manifest repletion, then prepare the patient to a good place for the operation; then remove your oncology or cancer, and shave off all hair, and take away from everywhere without leaving anything behind; let the blood run out completely, press the location well with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood opposes the incision made in an artery or vein, cauterize it so that bleeding stops; then treat them again until they are healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division about the similarities of dropsy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that can be achieved with medicines, and those cured by iron; so we will only write down [the latter]; one must not use iron for these two kinds: namely tympanites and ascites, because they are deadly things; therefore when you treat this dropsy called 'eclites' with medicine, and if the cure is not successful, then consider whether the patient is weak or suffering from another disease than dropsy, such as intestinal obstruction and similar conditions; do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient is of strong constitution, and they only suffer from dropsy without any other illness, and that he is neither too young nor too old, then proceed thus: lift the patient straight up with your hands, and have assistants press his belly while directing the water to the lowest part under the navel, then take the spathula sharp like this:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And it should be divided into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	A point, and yet it should not be so deep that it can reach the intestine when inserted, nor injure it; then look to see if the dropsy is connected towards the intestines: in this case you must make an incision above the navel three fingers directly below the waist; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the navel three fingers; and if it's for miuce, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie over the incision so that excess does not flow to this weak place; then pierce through all the skin with the instrument, insert [it] and lift your hand with a spatula between the skin and subcutaneous tissue as if you were skinning to the amount of one nail or around; then pierce the subcutaneous tissue until the spatula reaches an empty space, which is where water is located, pull it out, and place this instrument which has the following shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver cane, and made of light brass or iron, and on its lower part there is one small hole; and at the side in one place, three holes; and two on another side, and one more on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision that the physicians perform:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the handle, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it now descends onto the instrument; empty half or a third part, because if you empty more than necessary at this time, perhaps the patient will die due to the release of their spirit from the body, or they become lost, or approach death; but empty according to his strength, and according to what the state of the patient's strength indicates, and their pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now for the heart which blocks the hole that I have mentioned, which you pierce in this manner; then reintroduce the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering, and draw a small quantity of water; do this daily, and be careful not to leave even a little water inside.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient's condition, and you leave a lot of water inside them, then cure them with burial or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and prevent them from drinking; and treat them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize their stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stopping of the penis.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without an opening in their penis, or with a small one, or it is not correctly placed.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It should be pierced as soon as possible with a very thin spatula in this way:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put the subtle hollow reed of lead in place and bind it there for three or four days; when he wants to urinate, remove the tube so that he can urinate without impediment; then replace the tube afterwards; perhaps this is not necessary as the urine which will come out does not allow him to be closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those with a small tube will be treated by the leaden reed, as we have said, so that it widens.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose tube is not in its place become swollen because no one is born with the urethra at the head of their penis; that's why they cannot urinate unless they lift their penis upward and are unable to ejaculate since sperm cannot reach the glans, which is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is such that the patient often lies on their back; extend the head of the penis and the scrotum like the length of a feather, so that the opening faces upwards as it should; and beware of blood loss which occurs frequently, if this happens, stop the bleeding with whatever stops bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Pustules on the penis.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cist albathe frequently occurs on the penis and is an ugly appearing disease; there are malignant and non-malignant forms of this condition, so you must take a fine cautery tool to treat it, remove and clean all lesions, then apply wet cotton with Egyptian ointment; cure it using diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of foul colour and discharging, you must apply a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have incised it, and if the abscess is on a limb, with part of it beneath the skin and part outside, you must first remove the interior abscess; and when it is united, treat what remains outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, the limb of the affected area is not assured that it will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption occur in the affected limb and the penis; you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made from honey and flour with pomegranate bark and fig leaves, then cure it with other treatments until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is a loss of blood, apply the lunar cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterizations help with two conditions together: that is, the loss of blood and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you must insert a lead pipe into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin at the tip of the penis peels off, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or due to injury or abscess, then you must remove the skin with an instrument until the ligaments are loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a difficult matter to distinguish, then you must peel it with a spatula at the top part of the penis and its skin; then separate carefully between them, and apply a soft linen cloth dampened in cold water, so that it does not dry out again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like the detachment of continuity as other wounds are; nevertheless, when we perform this work by our own will and especially on children, it is necessary that we do our best and lightest work for their well-being.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children because it was not practiced in their law, and we only have this practice through our own experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen most masters and surgeons performing circumcision around the glans penis, and forcefully with one knife; it was their choice because there are two layers of skin there, and sometimes they cut the upper layer leaving the lower one intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, and the pain is doubled, and at the cleansing that comes from it isn't secure to point out of member; and in the cleaning of the nail perhaps escapes iron, and run work, and many times they arise thus that they don't need cleaning and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the cleansing that is done by force with all the thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, you cut equally in I all its tension; but let the thread be well narrow around the skin; and the way of the first work is that you make believe the child, if he understands, that you don't make him do anything more than tie the thread around the rod just so, and then you can make him sit in any way you want; then make him stand between your hands straight up, and hide the forces between your hands or below your feet so the child doesn't see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and blow on the heart, and pull it upwards until the head of the rod is inside; then clean it well from the dirt that has gathered there, then tie the place with a single thread, then bind it below I peg to another binding; hold it by II fingers using the second bandage at the thumb and index finger, cut between the two bindings, lift up the heart quickly and pull out the head of the rod; then let blood come out drop by drop because this is the corruption; put powder on top and over the powder a piece of linen stuck with half an egg cooked tempered in rose water, mixed with good fresh red oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure him with other cures until he is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of scissors for cleaning is as follows: the two blades should be inclined and sharp, and they should be as wide as the handle equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of cleaning is when the heart inside escapes through the incision; therefore, you must extend it to your nail, otherwise, the skin will form an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, then use pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is below the handle is swollen, leave it until the hot abscess subsides, and lightly peel it; cut it as much as you can, taking care of the part of the handle, this will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the location of things welding a wound with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if it scars beyond measure, and it rises above the skin, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	for retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is caused by obstruction due to stones, or frozen blood, or a tumor, or birth defect, or similar issues, as we have mentioned in the classification; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone blocking the bladder neck, then the patient must be bent over their knees; place their feet on their back, extend their belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's loins as much as possible; thereby compressing the bladder neck for the expression of the stone upwards, thus the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must perform extraction with all the instrument which is called a 'syringe', this is its form: it is made of fine silver, light-weight like bird feathers; the barrel is one palm long and half wide, and it has a fine point.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, and bottle the chief dou fill deadens the syringe; and cope the superfluiteit of the lainne and the bottle jusc'au chief of the syringe, then oint the syringe with oil or butter and with yolk of egg, and let the patient sit on a seat, and anoint his bladder and virile member with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then insert the syringe gently into the virile member until it reaches the root of the virile member, then double the virile member towards its orifice; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and let the patient feel when his thing is empty; but this is not done according to this order except because he who goes in there has a twist; then stretch the string at all the woolen pocs and pocs, and urine follows the wool, then take it out, and make the urine flow; and resume the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and let the patient be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	For bladder diseases.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scalding or blood enters the bladder, and there is a gathering of pus, if you wish to introduce distilled water and medicine into it, then use an instrument called a "clepsydra," which has this form:

The tube should have such a diameter that it fits tightly around the verge without any addition so that moisture cannot be drawn in, but rather expelled when necessary. When you want to introduce your medicine into the bladder, place the end of the tube into the liquid, draw up the contents by pulling on the attached cord; this will cause liquids to flow through the tube and into the bladder, which the patient will feel as it happens. This is a description of the subtle enema instrument with which one can administer an enema to the bladder: here is its form.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	Et est d'argent ou d'archaut, and it is the head higher; and below at the chest where the shoulder joint falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you want to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts firmly with a good double thread, and heat the pot with this moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the clyster into the penis, then press your hand over the bladder so that all the liquid passes, until the patient feels that this liquid has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle out of it, and pierce it round about; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then join the circle as one joins a thimble, put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; do likewise with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the liquid reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their extraction along with medicines; I have explained the difference between kidney stones and all the signs, and which stones require surgical removal; as well as those in the bladder and urethra; now I will explain it clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	The stone that is formed in the bladder occurs more frequently in children, and its sign is urine similar to water in subtlety; it produces sand, and the patient experiences frequent urination, and then becomes blocked; often this causes inflammation of the genitals; and there are many symptoms in children under four years old, while it is a serious condition for the elderly, and average for young adults between youth and old age; and treatment is easier for those with larger stones than for those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the bile that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes it blocks while seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, make him stand and move backwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from above; then have him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely declined downwards; then seek for it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in this space, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall out upon being touched at all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is an adult; and insert it into his anus, seek for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, lead it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the spatula cutting instrument, which has this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Make an incision between what is between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side; and let it be straight over the stone, and your fingers should be next to or near the anus, and make the incision wide on the outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, but not too large; perhaps the pressure will require that the finger at the anus is removed so there is no obstruction; and know that there are stones with angles and edges: it is difficult to remove; and those which are below, resembling a pea, and round, with a slight opening.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; 
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, one must take care of it and make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes back through an opening that the flesh cannot heal; nonetheless, try to drain it, or break it up with forceps, until you extract it in pieces; and when you have finished your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, bind it tight, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to ease the hot abscess; then lay the patient on their back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie it, thoroughly wash the wound with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of saffron and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses develop in the wound and there are blood clots in the bladder, causing urine retention which is known to occur in such a way that it comes out with urine: therefore, insert your finger into the wound, extract this blood, for if it remains, it will rupture the bladder and cause infection; then wash the wound with water, ash and salt, and treat it in all ways you know until it is healed; and ensure every time you treat him that you tie his two thighs together and apply medication to the site.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra, blocking the passage of urine which cannot come out; so heal him as I say, cut him many times, you are excused from cutting by this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod forged in this shape, with three angled prongs like a pitchfork.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft below the stone so that it cannot retreat into the bladder; next insert the rod gently up the shaft until you reach the stone; turn the rod in your hand within the stone back and forth, until you can pierce through to the other side. Thus will urine come quickly, then press your hand upon that which remains of the stone inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is quickly broken and passes with the urine, then the patient will be healed; if you cannot do this due to any obstruction, tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then make an incision in the shaft near the stone between these two lines, extract the rod, untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood from the wound; treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Before a stone is formed in women, and if it happens once, the cure is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that you cannot find a suitable woman who will expose herself to the doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third reason is that perhaps you cannot find an expert woman in this medical art; and the fourth reason is that the stone of a woman is usually deeper than that of a man, which requires a more profound incision, and there is great fear involved. If necessity arises for this, then you must take a wise midwife, and if you do not easily find one, seek a skilled and chaste female assistant; and present to her a well-behaved woman in the knowledge of women's health, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to carry out your examination for the stone; carefully check if the woman is a virgin: then insert your finger into her anus and search for the stone; if she finds it, force it underneath your finger, and instruct her to insert her finger inside the patient, and press your left hand firmly on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know these signs, you will understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the blood defeats you, quickly place crushed vitriol powder on it and hold for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, ensuring the stone is fully passed, and have the tools I mentioned for extracting stones from men ready to assist you in your task; and if the blood defeats you again, and it is the artery that is cut, apply the powder to the wound along with tent and bandage extracts, do not attempt this procedure again, leave the stone inside, otherwise the patient may die; treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has cooled and the wound is ready to be handled, return to your work, so that the stone may pass.
de hernie carnouse	A hernia of fleshy material
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Rattish water is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white puss, which is underneath the heart of calves and contained in eggshells; it is called "puss", and sometimes is found properly inside the egg itself, such that people believe this to be another egg entirely; rather, it's the calfskin between what we've described as white puss.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this rattish water comes from weakness in calves, and that matter is widespread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from striking calves and this moisture takes on many colours: it can be yellowish-brown, reddish, black or white puss, there are more as well; these signs will tell you what the matter is because if it's the white pus we've described then the abscess forms a round shape like an egg and doesn't break open the calves skin due to moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the wound itself, then the abscess comes out with a piece of egg white (pus), and for this reason it is thought to be another egg; but if the moisture is between the hide of calves and the white membrane (of an abscess), you can feel it well. Therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all kinds of intrusions before, as already explained above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the intrusion, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with an iron instrument, the patient should be bled according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on something slightly raised, and put a lot of cloth under him; then sit on his left side, and ask the assistant to sit on his right, extending the limb towards one of the two sides of the calf's heart. Then take the spatula, cut through the hide along its length until you reach the wrist, making your incision straight as you peel back the hide all the way down to the white membrane; carefully remove it according to your skill; then pierce this membrane full of water with a wide opening and extract all of the water, after which put in your hooks, stretching the membrane upwards. Do not touch the heart but only the membrane: cut it into pieces especially its thin side since if you do not separate them cleanly enough, water will return. And should egg white have been released during your operation, place it back where it came from once you've finished working on the membrane; then sew together the two sides of the hide with a stitch, treating it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, you must bind the suspending vessels, fearing blood loss; then cut all of the surrounding tissue, extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is gathered into two parts together, know that these are two roots; cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and place on the wound moist wool with rose oil; put over this another piece of wool moistened with wine and oil, and cover both orifices, putting doubled linen cloths above them, and bind all together with a bandage in this manner:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two pieces of linen, and fill them with wool charpie in this shape so that they are joined by stitching at the waist of the breeches; one of these place under the foundation up to the back, and the other at the arm part; and the other two above the angles, and all is joined together by the binding strap in this buckle manner; sometimes it happens that cauterization is used on this root instead of iron cutting; then you take a slender surgical knife as cautery, cut through the skin over the orifices, warming it so that the white substance containing the water is uncovered; then with this cautery shaped like this, pierce this white membrane at the corners and scrape out this delicate hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And strike it in all the ways you can, until everything is uprooted; be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; know that this work is safer; and take care of blood loss, and treat as if they were surgical operations; and if anything goes against you, whether an abscess gets hot or bleeding occurs or something else, then treat what opposes you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and does not want to undergo this procedure due to its horror, then you can induce perforation as I have told you; when you are certain of the water's presence through the signs we mentioned, have the patient sit on an elevated seat; make a puncture in the abscess below any muscle which covers it entirely, and insert the instrument lengthwise into the body; let the holes be wide so that all the fluid can flow out; then place cotton wool where you made the incision, bind it up, and leave it for the rest of the water to drain out, then treat until the wound is clean; if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to exit at the mouth of the wound, you must insert a quill or the instrument used to draw off water from dropsical patients (of which we have already given the shape); enlarge this hole in the wound and know that the fluid will return after six months or so, and when it is gathered as before, so will pass these days for the patient.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of abscesses of the jaw
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the treatment of this issue there is fear in many situations, which makes it seem better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, especially in the jaw; and this is due to frequent cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known to be caused by excess acidity and bile, which spreads to the jaw, or due to impact; and the colour of the abscess matches that of the body; and there is no pain, but it is a deep abscess; and perhaps some abscesses are painful, hard, and discoloured, and sometimes arise from an artery, or from swollen veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is caused by an arterial wound, it is recognized as a hot abscess due to its warm texture when you press it with your fingers; and you must not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	One who suffers from swelling of the vein is recognized by its appearance when touched with fingers, and one can easily perform surgery on this type of swelling as well as other types; it involves cutting out the heart of the tumor, then stretching the skin upwards, and removing the white part, thereby freeing the swollen area from all parts of the tumor.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the tumor is already hardened with its own skin, you must therefore remove the tumor and cut it out; and if it is aerated on the surface or inside vessels, then you must release all that tension and cut around it smoothly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is from behind, you must cut it all away and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once your work is complete, cover the wound with wet wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
de l’aposteme des coions	of carbuncles on the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a carbuncle wrapped in an envelope like the seed of a thistle, with a softening of the buttocks, and the patient turns very ill when he defecates; and the treatment for this illness is just as fearful as the one before, yet we will tell you how to treat it according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then tie the hanging strap of the testicles around your thumbs, grasping all vessels near the penis and holding them firmly; stretch it well; then cut across these vessels with a broad cutting spatula until they are uncovered, and skin each side as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples; insert a needle where there is double thread, tie it at the first point where the vein has been punctured, and retie it to the other end; then cut them straight across in the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove corrupted tissues; cure the wound like others that involve bowels so that no vessel prevents the blood supply from one testicle; because this way there is not risk of harm, but if all vessels are punctured, you must pull out both testes: in order for the urethra to lose its blood supply through the incision of the vessels, it dries up and cannot be cured.
de la routure dou syfac	From the rupture of the syfac
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this rupture is due to the section that opens into the syfac, or the extension on the belly in the region of the intestines, which causes the intestines to descend from this rupture towards one of the hips; and this rupture occurs either in the syfac itself or in its extension, arising from two types of excessive strain: percussion, jumping, sneezing, lifting heavy loads, and similar activities; when it is due to the extension of the syfac, there are signs that it develops slowly over a long period without suddenly occurring; the abscess becomes equalized towards the peritoneum because the syfac presses against the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	The signs are that when it is due to the section of the syfac, it causes sudden pain at first, and the abscess appears diverse under the skin close by; this is because of the exit of the intestine and its body outside the syfac.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines descend with the bowels, becoming entangled there, causing great pain to be endured by the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron treatments with fear, it is necessary to withdraw from them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	The manner of the procedure is such that you instruct the patient to retract the intestines with their hand into the wound if they can reach it; then be mindful of its position on his neck between your hands, and lift their thighs; then stretch out the heart above, and cut all the skin from the lower abdomen along the length; then push inside the scissors of the abdomen as much as you need to open the wound, and make it such that the wind can escape through it; then peel off the white membrane underneath the skin of the testicles until the hard white membrane is exposed on all sides; then push your index finger into what covers the testes, between the white membrane which lies beneath the scrotal skin, and between the second membrane, and remove that which lies behind the testis, and between the second membrane; and with your right hand inside the abdomen of the testes, stretch out the white membrane upward to your left hand, and lift the testis along all its surface towards the abdomen; and command the assistant to stretch out the testis upwards, and untie that which is tied behind; and look for yourself if there are any intestines wound up in the hard white membrane, and if you find anything, push it down into the belly below; then take a needle with thread as thick as ten threads, and push it through the rear part of the membrane, after the scrotal skin, towards the abdomen, then cut the testicles which appear from the threads until there are four threads; then assemble one on top of another in the manner of a cross, and tie them together to the hard white membrane underneath the scrotal skin with a strong double knot; then wind the threads around the testicles, and tie them firmly in two parts so that none of the vessels which nourish them can enter anywhere near it where an abscess could form; and re-tie along the first long thread from end to end of one hand's length, and after these two ties leave a membrane underneath the heart of the testes the size of a finger; and afterwards, cover all according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part beneath the scrotal skin until the blood and bile flows out, as we have said before; then apply moist wool with oil to the wound, and reapply the thread which we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white skin is cauterized as we have said, after incision, out of fear of profuse bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens often, and leave the bandage until it falls off by itself; and if it delays in falling, then be bathed with warm water, and apply what we have said until it falls; then treat the wound with another remedy until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernia cruris.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this infirmary, I have never seen anyone dare to treat it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is treated like the infirmary which is together with the stomach, in such a way that you tie the vessels after cutting above them lightly underneath; then cut into the middle, and treat the abscess of what causes harm, until the vessels fall out; and treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.
