When rupture occurs in the groin, as we have mentioned, the tissue becomes exposed; and no part of the intestines descends to the scrotum, if it does descend there is little, and it repairs itself every hour; however, if it remains too long at this stage, the wound or hernia grows until the intestine descends; and this happens due to the extension of the hernia in the groin, as we have stated earlier, because it extends then becomes soft, swollen, and exposed; its cure is by cauterization, as mentioned before; sometimes cured with iron like this: make the patient lie on his back often between your hands, cut open the swelling at the rupture site widely according to three fingers size; remove the hernia that is under the skin that covers it then take a rod and put it over the visible part of the hernia; push it towards the abdomen bottom then cut the two sides of the hernia's surface on top of the rod, one side after another; take out the head of the rod without cutting any part of the hernia or extending the egg or other things as I made you aware in the cure of intestinal prolapse; afterwards treat by treating wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat a wound on boys, clean it well and heal the wound until it is completely cured.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The knife is appropriate here, but it has no effect on the wound opening up, and cauterization is more effective in this place, being closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the skin of the calves
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the calves is softened in some people because the flesh underneath is softened and can be seen through it; and when one wants to treat it, they must make the patient lie on their back, then cut away the soft skin over the natural skin; next join the two edges together with a stitch, if you wish, first cut off the superfluous part of the soft skin into three or four folds securely; then cut between the stitches and cure it like other wounds until it is healed and the thread removed.
dou chastrement	The castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castrations are forbidden in our law, and for this reason, I would prefer not to discuss them in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is so the surgeon can know how to respond when asked about it and knows the cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate some animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, cattle, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castrations are performed in two ways: either by extraction or incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the case of those we perform by extraction, make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles are softened and hanging down; then grasp them with your hand until they retract and you can no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastrement de taille: you must hold the animal down and press its testicles with your left hand, then tie a cord around them, cutting each one once when they have been properly crushed; leave some of the tunics as well as the fine membrane that covers the vessels intact since this kind of castration is less harmful than that which is done by crushing, because something may possibly be left in the testicles from the crushing process, causing the animal to retain its desire for sex. Then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	D'hermaphroditis: of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites occur in two ways among humans; the first is that between the testicles appears something like a woman's genitalia, with hair and sometimes it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it has on the wrist like a rod and two knobs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	The treatment for men and women is such that you cut all the adhering parts together, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the knobs, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	Of stinging nettle.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Stinging nettle is an adhering part on the natural body part, so ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of the nettle in your hand or with tongs, and cut it lightly; do not go too deep, lest blood flow out, then treat any other wound until it is healed; and for another growth that appears at the edge of the vulva, remove it, and perhaps it will be sore, and it looks like a cow's udder, so the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it off just as we said for the abscess, and treat it until it is clean.
de erratique	Of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the woman's nature is not pierced, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident due to illness that has occurred; or it is caused by a charred adjustment, or subtle surgical procedure, or species, and it occurs perfectly in the uterus, or on its sides, or beneath, wherever it may be; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps even menstruation; and knowledge of such a case is determined by examination of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the obstruction is close and apparent, apply pressure with your fingers or use an instrument.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is so subtle that it has reached the two lips, hurry and do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two lips wide apart, so that the subtle syfac is exposed, and cover the opening; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and make the woman lie with a man every day until it cannot close.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syfac is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatule similar to myrtle leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the opening is made of new wood, suspend it with a hook and cut it; and have the medicines for stopping bleeding, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then provide a wide copper tube so that the wound cannot close; and let this persist for some time, and give her dry linen thread; then treat her with other cures until she is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a child is born dead, you must cut it up according to this method, unless there are deep-rooted abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess which is deeply rooted in the womb, one should not make any incisions.
des emorroides	Of haemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Haemorrhoids are open wounds where blood usually flows freely, and when haemorrhoids become old they turn into small bumps or lumps; I have previously mentioned their similarities to others, and the signs, and now I will tell you which ones can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that haemorrhoids and small bumps or lumps, when they are located deep within the rectum, and cannot be felt externally, cannot be treated with cautery.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, where one can feel it, those are the ones that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore put the woman in a cold house, then extend the ulcer with pincers, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, such as dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if there is subsequent bleeding, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, galls, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and make an ointment which you apply to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have the patient cup their back and breasts without harm; then take linen, dampen it in juice of plantain or elderberry with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, must be cut away as I said for the thelul; then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the gums
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many forms of abscess arise in the gums, such as cancer, stony abscesses, herpes, warts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have described previously.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which appears on the buttock, which is not one of the abscesses that pierce; and if you wish to know how to treat it, look to see if the abscess is acute at its onset, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, and provide two small seats for them to lean against, supporting their back and bringing their feet up towards the outside of their legs; their thighs should be spread apart, and they should place their arms underneath their knees, tying them securely with a good bandage. Then suck out the contents towards the right side, and bring in the instrument used to open the mouth of the abscess, from which comes its shape; when you use this instrument, it is necessary that you first mark a line to determine the depth of the abscess so that what enters does not go deeper than it should and cause injury. If your instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the abscess with cloth, ensuring the instrument doesn't harm the patient; the operator must place their horn at the top and hold onto the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is treated with a hot iron, you must be careful to avoid burning; instead, treat it as we have described in our previous instructions.
de l’enfantement	Childbirth.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is essential for the midwife to understand the process of natural childbirth and its signs, such as when you see the woman pushing downwards and feeling the urge to bear down: then the child is ready to emerge quickly. Understand that these labours are natural, with the baby's head presenting first, followed by assistance from those helping; and when you witness these indicators, gently push on her belly so the child can exit swiftly; for once it descends upon its head, help is required, and the womb will expel its excesses through proper purification. Those born differently do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes happens that he falls on his feet, and the body comes down onto his shoulders or hands, or it may land on his stomach, often even on to his neck, and in other bad positions; therefore, it is necessary for her to be wise and skillful in these matters, and avoid error and deception, and I shall show you all the ways in which she must help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out onto his head due to natural causes, and the woman gives birth with great difficulty, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a saddle or be held by the women; apply some warm oil of fenugreek to her nature, and then insert the small spatula between her two fingers as shown here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the amniotic sac, and trim her nail so that the moisture which is there flows out; press on her belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must give the woman an enema of fenugreek with sesame oil; make her sneeze using ground cumin, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands emerge first, you must gently reposition them little by little; and if they cannot be reinserted, then place the woman on a seat, lifting her feet in the air; next, lower the seat to the ground, holding onto the woman so she does not fall during lowering; and if the hands still cannot be inserted, and the child is dead, then cut open the hands with the knife provided here, extracting the child, and reposition evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the emergence of the child's feet.
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child arrives at its feet, you must push it upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is even; next, take one foot and stretch it out little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When it reaches the thighs, instruct them to grab hold, and make them sneeze strongly; if it has escaped, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it has not escaped as we said, turn it back and forth until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is only slightly dislocated.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we said, take a little mucilage of alum, and oil of turpentine, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; spread this ointment inside and outside the affected part, then make her sit in warm water up to below the ribs; when she is softened below, make a myrrh collar for her, place it underneath, and let it remain for an hour; then have her sit on a seat, make her sneeze, and hold her mouth and nose shut while gently pressing her belly because the child will now come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	On the birth of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes into this world, place the midwife's hands upon it here and there; then let her lay her hand on its neck, and hang his feet downwards while he lies on the bed; then let her fold his hands in a certain way, and press them to his stomach, and remove the cushions from beneath him until he is prepared for what follows; if the child cannot do this himself, take hold of his feet and move them forcibly; next push up his stomach with your hand, finally insert all four fingers; then wash the child here and there; and tell the mother to grasp the child while it comes forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	On the birth of a child that is larger than normal with an arm hanging out.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise a way to bring back the hand: if you cannot do it, make her stand and walk; if she can't walk, have her lie on the bed, with her legs spread apart; then apply the poultice I mentioned; if she doesn't give birth, sit her on a chair, try to bring back the hand; take care of the child according to nature's pattern, make her sneeze, and tell her to catch the baby when it comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	On the birth of the child onto her neck, spread out her hands, with her face turned towards the back of her mother's.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	The nurse should hold her hand and turn it over and over, lifting it lightly until it is even; apply a natural poultice of flour and oil as mentioned earlier, telling her to move slowly; after you have done this, sit her on a chair again, tell her to catch the baby when it comes out and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this very same manner to all of the secondary [joints]
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes loose in this manner to all of the secondary [joints], cut the second one with your nail until the moisture is drained; and if the child can crawl on their face and neck, grasp them from below so that they are not trapped, then kill the child; push the infant inside as you must, and instruct the woman not to move: then deliver gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four come at once; this is not strange, and it does happen.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Those are strange things, and they do not live, if you ask me; I know that they multiply, and they are separated by the healing touch which divides them, which is bound to the swelling; and sometimes they also come out naturally like a worm, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they come out severely, then treat it as we have said, and let the physician be skilled, and act swiftly and gently in what she does; and do so as is best for healing.
de plusors enfans	Of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child by the measurement of God's glorious blood, and it is necessary that the physician knows all this, for perhaps similar things will happen to him; so he should act accordingly as needed.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child in her womb, as I mentioned earlier, and there is no progress made, and you are forced to intervene physically; it is essential that you ascertain whether the woman possesses sound virtue, and she has not suffered any accident nor fears death; the woman should be laid on her back with her hips inclined downward, and her legs lifted; the assistant should hold her from two sides, or she should be tied in bed so as to prevent movement during the procedure. The mouth of the deceased child's mother is then rubbed with moist oils mixed with an infusion of althea and fenugreek seeds, and linseed oil is applied to the palms of her hands; these oils are gently inserted into the woman's vagina, ensuring that the position of the unborn child is suitable for this procedure. Take caution if the fetus is positioned on its head during descent, insert the fetoscope into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or beneath its beard or in its fontanelle or near its sides; and if the fetal descent occurs via its feet, place the fetoscope at its navel or median sulcus; it should be held by your right hand, with the curve of the instrument placed between the fingers of your left hand, gently inserted into one of the aforementioned places until the fetus is completely extracted. This is the form of the fetoscope:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place it against the other handle, or use a third if needed to ensure equal extraction; and then extend them equally by moving from one side to the other, so that they may be removed, and let the handles be serrated to hold them in place, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, have the surgeon oil his fingers and push them into that area, then pull out the other part; but if there are no remaining fragments, place this handle higher up and repeat until it is all removed.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes out before the other and you cannot retract it due to constriction, wrap them both in a cloth until they are entirely covered; then cut through the joints of the palms or at the wrist, and do likewise for the other hand and foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is standing on their feet, the traction is light, and the adjustment at the mouth of the wound is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If he is constricted in the belly or chest, you must extract him with cloth wrapped around your hand; and split open his belly or chest as far as necessary to remove the moisture that has accumulated there; and if other organs have been dislocated but the head remains inside, insert your hand perfectly into the wound and pull it down towards the mouth of the wound; then insert one or two fingers, and pull them through forcefully. And if the mouth of the wound is narrow due to hot inflammation which has developed within, you must not exert force thereon, but rather administer moist and fatty substances such as emollients and softening poultices in water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side and you can lay it flat, proceed as we have described for a living child; but if not, then take it apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth behind.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	Once you have done this, proceed as we described for hot abscesses that appear in the armpit; if blood flows from the incision, immerse it in cold water and apply pressure, then treat with other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly contained one dead child, then another grew on top of it, but the other died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the throat and swelled until it burst, beginning to rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat him, and I thought long, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster of strong attraction, and an bone came out, then after some days another one followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised for the abdomen has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these must be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and extracted several bones from it until the woman felt much better; and thus the woman lived for a long time with only a small lump in its place; and I have not remembered this chapter except that when masters encounter strange cases, they should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To move the swelling back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the compress, with which one has strips of cloth; and returning to the second head of two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more slender than the constrictor, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the trunk is two fingers wide, and the width of the tree bark is one finger, and it is a palm and half long; and in the middle of the two lines are two fittings of this same wood, which are firmly attached to each other, with a length of half a palm or slightly more; these two fittings are placed into the mouth of the swelling to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more slender and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood like a pair of pliers; it has two heads with two fittings as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; when you want to open the swelling with this whole instrument, have the woman sit on a bed, feet hanging down and legs apart, then insert the two fitted parts together into the swelling, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then operate your hand with the whole instrument as you did with the pliers equally according to the amount that you want to open the mouth of the swelling until the pain is relieved.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you don't despair of the instrument that you haven't prepared, because its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the labor is prolonged for childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze forcefully, and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she faints from this, it's good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make a hole in its lid, then put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; cook all these herbs or some of them in water over fire; then place one end of the pipe into the pot and the other into the mouth of the womb, holding it so that the vapors go inside the womb; then make her sneeze, as we said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the injury happens during labor.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not come out easily, instruct the midwife to wet her left hand in oil of sesame or muskroot juice, then insert it into the birth canal, and seek the retained placenta. When she finds it, she should grasp it gently and extend it little by little, so as not to hinder its extraction; but she must move it lightly from side to side before pulling it out. This will cause it to come away easily.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the passage of the birth canal is narrow, we have mentioned the treatment of inducing sneezing and herbal fumigation; but if it does not work despite all these measures, then take care not to force extraction; instead bind what is at the mouth of the womb to the thigh of the woman, then give her a clyster with four-ingredient ointment. This will ripen and prepare [the birth canal], and it will open up; but still, when she does deliver, there may be bad odor in the stomach and head, which can harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So you must apply appropriate fumes for this, some of the ancients have tried vapors from watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the tool with which one fumes the woman to retain flowers and the afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass resembling a dog's shape, and one puts the subtle head into the natural place, and the wide ends on the fire; and let the fumes be above the coals, and let the rag be wasted until it is gone, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without a pierced fundament, but rather it is stopped with a subtle plug: so during the bath you must pierce this plug yourself, and do not use an acute probe, being careful that she is not touched; then place soft wool soaked in wine and oil on top, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, insert a plank wedge into the hole and leave it there for several days; remove it when the child wishes to go outside.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Sometimes this healing occurs suddenly in a wound or abscess; it is necessary to cut through the scabs, so that they are cured just as we have said of the plank wedge.
de la fistule dou fondement	From the fistula of the anus.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from beneath the anus are called nodations, and growths coming from outside the anus in the space between two parts have a fistula or more; when this nodation is old, it becomes moist, and white or subtle pus forms around it, sometimes these fistulas perforate; they're recognized by what comes out during defecation or flatulence — maybe some worms come out too.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And so for fistulas that reach down to the bladder, and halfway up the penis; they extend right up to the hip socket, and all the way around the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus you can know the fistula piercing through the anus, and not just piercing: it is that you insert your index finger into the anus, and gently push a thin needle made of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, then insert a slender tent made of lead or a horsehair, until you can feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you cannot feel it, and no excretion, wind or feces come out as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so do not hasten to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is perforated up to the bladder or up to the urinary tract, then urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the hip joint, then the wound reaches that place; if there is no tortuosity and the source of pain is found nearby, then one must go directly for surgery, and neither medicine nor quick treatment with ointments will help; in such perforating fistulas, there is no cure but hard work, and the foolish pride of quack doctors who meddle.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In those cases where it is not perforated and not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have proven, and the patient must lie between your hands on their back; lift their legs up to their thighs, and incline their thighs towards their belly; then insert a bronze probe, or a lead one if there is tortuosity, until you know where the probe goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, you must put your index finger inside, if you then feel that the tendon is pierced; and if uncovered where you can feel between your finger skin or flesh, know that it is perforated; do not work on it until it can be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says however that one can heal some of them well, but this happens rarely; and the aid it provides is such that you heat a subtle cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before; and insert it hot into the fistula until it reaches near the anus; do this II or III times until you know that these faulty fleshes are burned which resemble bird feathers; then treat it with wet bandages in butter so that all flesh is removed, and then heal it with a soothing ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus cured, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be cured in any other way; and if the probe enters, but does not reach the bone at the base, and between your probe and the probe is a thick covering of flesh or sinew, and you see the fistula from which the cover erupts like heartwood; then cut away the start of the fistula, push forward with the probe, and cauterize afterwards until you reach the head of the probe; and the probe will be released and fall out; then clean those defective flesh parts that look like a bird's feather, leaving nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood rushes forth between you and the operation, then cauterize with fire or astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cauterization with fire combines two beneficial effects: namely, burning away adjacent flesh, and staunching blood flow while drying out moisture; then treat moist wounds with butter or ground substances until the wound heals, once the charred flesh has healed over in the bowels; then treat a weeping sore with caustic ointments hardening tough flesh, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula reaches all the way to the anus, and is distant from the body, then insert your finger into the anus and ask them.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the wound, and find there is skin or membrane or flesh where it is about to burst open, and have no hope of healing except through one of these three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut deeply until reaching bone, or if possible apply an ointment and treat it like before; and do not go too deep lest you sever the muscle holding together the anus, causing involuntary defecation; then treat as we have described previously; perhaps the wound will be healed without further action; otherwise remove this skin cover and clean it after cutting it away from around the anus, with a compress or other sharp instrument; next remove any faulty flesh remaining in the wound as much as possible; finally consider restoring the wound and blocking off the fistula below the anus: which would cause less distress for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas form in this manner: it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it sits against the wall near the inner skin above, take a pierced tent at its head shaped like this:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And here you insert the thread twisted into it in such a way that when you put the tent through the entire thread into the fistula, it should be at its head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the edge of the inner foundation, then withdraw the thread from that hole so you can put your finger inside the foundation; pull the head of the thread and bring together the two heads, holding them tightly to one another for a day or two; sometimes hold it until the thread binds these edges together causing discharge; finally treat the wound until it is sealed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, make it burst by all means you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to cut for the lacing if it is too deeply embedded, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spinalis muscle from which the fistula is made is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and for this reason, you do not cut what must not be cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	Of haemorrhoids.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Haemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and they bleed a little; and sometimes there is one or several, and they come out from the anus and at the top of the anus. But those that appear outside have very little moisture, but rather some yellow water or blood, and are the colour of flesh. The treatment for these inside the anus is as follows: you must instruct the patient to strain themselves in order to defecate, until the faeces leave them so that their buttocks open up; then they should hurry and use forceps on it, or hold it with your fingernail, then cut into its roots. And if the hooks cannot hold them due to moisture, you can take them by a piece of cloth or cotton wool or a small piece of chamois leather, and extract them with two fingers; then treat them either by applying some warm powder instead of cauterising, or treat them as described in the chapter on cauterisation. You may also cure them using other treatments until they are healed. And if the anus cannot open up, you should give the patient a sharp enema to clean out what is inside the anus so that it can be easily opened. When the patient strains and their buttocks open up, then treatment is easier; and this consists of holding them with your fingernail or forceps, cutting into them, treating as described above until they are healed, avoiding any incision by iron instrument.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you must perform a suture in this way: take one twisted thread and insert it into a needle; then pull the thread through from above and make the needle pierce on the other side; turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let them be wide; tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, withdraw the needle, and do likewise for all others; leave one in place to allow excess blood to flow out; then apply over the wound a moistened piece of fabric soaked in rose oil or cerate, and put it on the wound, telling the patient to rest; leave them like this until they evacuate [the affected area], then treat with ointment and other treatments until healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryness of the faeces or wound
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is constipation of faeces in the intestine, and due to the constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must cut back to the point of a spatumile or your nail's length into the bark above it, which should not be moist; then clean it until it is firm as it should be; and if it cannot heal, resume scraping more intensely than before, until it heals greatly, and becomes scarred; then clean it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small faulty appearance between the body, and go deep inside; sometimes it finds coldness, and one feels them trembling like death, and they come all over the body, but more on hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane made from a goose quill or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the trembling [part of the body], so that the purple circles touch the trembling all around; then turn your hand over the entire cane such that you grasp it all around the trembling, and push in completely, extracting the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you want, make something like this from a brass or iron cane according to this form, and have it hollow underneath but solid on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, in order to hold it with two fingers and squeeze; And if you want, cauterize the trembling, as described in the previous chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	One never performs a clyster with silver or mercury, or melted bronze or wire; and one makes these instruments both small and large, according to what they are adapted for.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which one adapts in the treatment of children and those who are weak and suffer pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster both small and large is thus broadly tied to the belly according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has a fastening by which the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is perforated within; and it has on one side two perforations, and on the other one; and let the belly where the medicine is placed be made of either animal bladder or parchment, and be perforated all around with tiny holes, and have between each hole one finger's breadth, then insert into these holes a strong thread made of raw silk twisted in an X shape or woven round, and join together the belly like that of a goat; and when the medicine is within, tie it to the instrument before with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the circular form:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicament be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the syringe with oil or egg white, or something similar, then insert it gently; next have the ministers press his two hands together, until he is all bared, then remove the syringe, and raise the patient's legs to the wall, and if the medicament wishes to exit, hold him as much as you can; and if he sleeps a night through, it is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you syringe him with a dislodgement of the belly illness, and the medicament hastens to exit, repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or abscess, let the syringe be as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of the gentle syringe with which the skin is tightened.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed the treatment of wounds; now we shall tell you about the practice of surgery and medicine, according to its completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, where the wounds are located, and what causes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various things such as blows from a stone, sword cuts and stabs with knives or lances, or strikes from sticks or arrows, or similar objects; wounds can also be classified according to the body part affected like a wound on the neck, head, foot, stomach, liver, and other limbs. I will tell you about the treatment of each kind of wound, starting with simple head wounds since the rest will follow in their respective chapters.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, take note if it is due to a stone strike or similar incidents, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you have mild doubts of abscess heat: then make them bleed immediately with the cephalic vein especially if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite the injured part; and avoid the patient overindulging in wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they do not want to bleed, then reduce their meat intake, and drink no wine or eat any flesh; place on the wound, if hot abscesses appear, cotton moistened with rose oil only, or with astringent wine; but if there is no heat of abscess, apply instead to the fresh wound in its full blood, and it has not yet moved due to air exposure, the powder I will mention shortly; however, should it have begun to move from being exposed to air, then use some salves until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by means of stitches, then join them by sewing, as I shall explain for wounds in the belly, concerning suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposing bone, gaping open and only held together by a flap of skin, cut it away; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as liver and boiled wheat, chicken too, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find the skin is rotting and not yet down to bone, cut away all that is rotten, then throw it out; next treat the wound; but should there be a severed artery in the wound or vein, which will not stop bleeding despite treatment with medicines, tie off the artery, and should you locate its end frayed, stitch it closed with thread; yet if this proves unavailing, cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: it requires that you apply this powder which seals as soon as the arse has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and finely powder them; use it to dress the wound, holding it firmly in place until it dries well and joins with all its blood; then bind it tightly, leaving it without unbinding, if there is no swelling; for medicine should be removed only once it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes quicklime alone is used when there is no incense or dragon's blood available, but the arse must have moved over the wound first.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has burned the wound, especially in summer, do not apply this powder to it; but use some digestible ointments instead or a poultice made of barley flour with water and honey until it runs clear; then treat it further with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture occurs along with the wound, and it is minor, extract it with delicate pincers; I will tell you about skull fractures later.
de la plaie dou col	On the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound occurs on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no distinction between this and that of the head, but if the vein or artery in the neck is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the black one, there is no other treatment than to leave it be, and put nothing restrictive on it, for it harms nerves and makes them retreat; and do not place anything cold on the wound, as the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest organ; but let the medicine be mild, just like warm water washed in soft water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked lettuce also washed in soft water, and other stones of fine quality according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with hair and bowels, cut it at a lower level; and if the artery is severed, and blood flows out, expose it, clean it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the windpipe of the throat is severed, or the heart, and the conduit is preserved so that air can pass through, cut the heart above the root of the throat, but do not touch the throat itself, instead reset it according to its natural shape; then bind it appropriately, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with draining ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, pull out the ones you can, and those you cannot, let them remain until the wound becomes putrid, and keep the discharge light and unclogged; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle over it the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound with a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of the wounds from lances or knives.
