Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or knife and the injury is deep, examine whether wind escapes with each breath of the patient: know then that the wound is mortal. If it is not deep and remains fresh with all its blood, do not apply any powder nor bind it in the first hour lest the blood congeals inside the wound, returns to the heart, and kills the patient. But instead apply an attracting ointment and bandage twice a day; if you have no such ointment, place old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and let the patient sleep on their injury for three days or four or more so that they suffer no spasm nor painful palpitations of heart nor strange fits. And when you see these good signs know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it then with bandages and other treatments until it is healed; if it cannot heal, operate as you must for a fistula has formed there. Treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it is simple, whether on the chest, arm or back, then treat what is in front of you; if it is large, stitch it; if small, dust with powder; if pieces have penetrated into the bone and are wedged there, search for them in the wound and pull out the protruding ends if they are not already separated. If they are not separate let the wound rot so as to facilitate their extraction. For wounds on other parts of the body treat accordingly, as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	rupture of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupturing of the belly is extensive, moderate and small; in large wounds some times the intestines or the nerves of the intestines come out, which leads to liquid infiltration; and stitching it up is harder, and sometimes a smaller wound causes more issues than a larger one, because you need to put back all of the intestines slowly if not done from hot to cold; that's why a medium-sized opening is better as it allows easier repositioning of the intestines in their place. And know that abdominal rupture occurs four ways: two are general and common for stitching up the belly wound while two others are specific for other body wounds, but they can be used with more precision on the belly wound; I will explain each one separately
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and a part of the intestine has come out, and it is difficult to replace, this can be done in one of two ways: either due to the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it up in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth with tepid water only, or cook it in water infused with squill and cypress and spike, and bathe the intestine until the swelling is reduced; and sometimes use a constricting wine, which is mild and helps to reduce the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or cook mallow, as this eases entry a little; and if it cannot enter, make an incision in the wound using the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is mild so that no cutting should be done without great need, here are the instruments for splitting it: it cuts inside at the curve and outwards, see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have moved out of place, reposition them according to their natural form into their proper position if you are able, for this improves the situation.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide and located below the belly, you should make the patient lie on their back with their legs elevated above their head; if it is below the belly, place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; likewise, for a rupture in one of the two parts, ensure the affected part is positioned higher than the other. Thus must be administered what I say regarding large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use what is available to you; then with your hands place a gentle compress that covers the entire rupture in its palm; this is how sutures are commonly performed: take a needle or multiple ones according to the size of the wound's width, and leave two fingers' breadth at the top of the wound, and insert into it a good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with the siphac, which is beneath the skin inside, so that you pass through this part and gather together the two ends of the siphac in fours; then pull one end of double thread around the needle from two sides, assemble the two edges of the wound appropriately, and leave a two-fingers' breadth gap before inserting another needle. Tie off the thread as you have done with the first needle, continuing to repeat this process according to your needs with needles until the entire wound is closed; the needles must be medium sized, between fine and thick since the very fine ones cut through all the flesh, while the too large are unable to enter properly: thus they should be moderate in size. Do not push the needles beyond the surface of the skin and flesh as this would cut and reopen the wound before healing can take place; then clip off the ends of the needles so that they do not prick the patient when asleep, and cover their tips with cloth or rags to hold them in place until the wound has healed. This method of suturing with needles is more appropriate for smaller wounds since only one or two needles are required: the second kind of suture is common too; it involves gathering together both sides of the skin and siphac with a single needle that has strong medium-sized thread, and after piercing all four parts simultaneously pull the needle back to the part where you began in the same way cloth is sewn. Between each stitch leave an interval equal to the size of your smallest finger; this type of suture was used on me when I had a wound on my stomach caused by a knife cut that extended more than a palm's length, exposing intestines which were more than two palms wide, and the rupture was in the middle of my belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned his intestine after it had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed in fifteen days, I cured him, and he healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged him to die, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointments because I was in a place where none were found, nor any medicines; instead, I applied old cotton twice daily on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and push it from outside to in; once it has pierced through the heart from right to left, leave the tip of the needle on the skin where you pushed it, then make it pierce from another side, from inside to out; the understanding of this suture is that you sew like a furrier does furs, leaving one side of the wound open and taking up the other until the whole suturing is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, as Galen accurately describes it, is performed similarly to how some do it, by joining the two parts together naturally and bringing one end of the wound close to the other in such a way: insert a needle into one side of the wound near your hand, pierce only that spot, and leave both ends of the wound; then turn the needle and pass it through from the outside layer down to inside, towards the two ends of the wound; then pierce once more from the outer layer down to the inner for each of the other two sides of the wound on the far side; this is a similar method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen describes this as follows, and it is witnessed by many: the abdomen must be sewn with two needles, each having a thread attached; one needle should be inserted on one side of the wound and the other on the opposite side, in the manner of those who stitch leather straps; note that when the tear is located in the center of the abdomen, the stitching will be more difficult compared to other areas of the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those for other wounds: when you find the wound fresh and full of blood, whether the doctor has moved it or not, then stop the intestine from bleeding and sew up the cut; then apply a powder made from healing meat, and if the doctor has already moved it, then apply any appropriate ointment until the wound heals over; cauterize the strings, and suture the edges; then treat the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, as soon as it starts to heal over, put on old cotton, moving it twice a day until it's healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will lead to gangrene of the main parts of the body, then you must wet a light linen cloth with warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected area and under the armpits; and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, which often happens, then administer a mild enema of red wine, especially if the infection has spread to the intestine; make an incision within it, and know that when it's the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The gut which is called "bowel" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the shallowness of its veins, and because of the delicacy of the whole body, and the nearness of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the muscle springs from the wound, reset it like an intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned worm-like or black, then you must bind the area that is black, so no blood flows there, for veins and arteries are present; then cut away what lies between the bindings, and suspend both ends of them from below the wound outward to ease the extraction as the muscles fall, and let the wound open.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the breaking of the mouth.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw a man pierced in the belly by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from it issued waste matter and flatulence. I treated him according to my ability and did not cease until he was healed and the skin joined.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it healed, I feared the patient might have pain in their belly; and there was no pain, but he remained in good condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be treated as follows: take large-headed pins, then gather the lips of the wound together, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it clamps the opening shut. Then cut off the head of the pin so that it cannot come undone; after this, put another pin in the same way as before until the whole wound is held together; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever she might be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, once it begins to heal, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is covered and sunken.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is truly a faulty hard and white nodule, where one does not feel pain, and it is also covered like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it jumps clear and sunken, and other times thick; sometimes small, and others large; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and has no flesh, remains so due to only one of these nine causes: namely, the little blood or matter; or its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, preventing new flesh from growing; or there is too much sunken area; or the skin is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is not good; or due to a manner of pestilence causing corruption; or due to the nature of the region being slow at digestion, and thus late with healing, and prone to swelling; or there are veins or bones involved: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and medicinal cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now you must let me inform you of the treatment for fistula, which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula can occur in any part of the body; for there are fistulas that come to major veins, and arteries, and nerves, or on the skin, or in the intestine, or bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spine, or in a joint of hands or feet; and so it comes to the proper place of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of quick healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not reach its proper place as I have said, and you have faith in the treatment, and recognize it, take a probe of brass or iron, if the fistula is straight, search with it; and if the fistula is twisted, search for a subtle thin probe made of lead, because lead can bend to follow the twists; and if the fistula has multiple openings, and you cannot properly find it with probes, irrigate one opening, as moisture passes from one hole to another, and clean it; then diligently probe it with your hand, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and is entirely hairless, and carefully ask the patient of the pain he feels when pressed by your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly understand its place, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I told you, then treat according to what I have said, and remove all pus and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then heal the fistula so that it may be healthy, and if the fistula is deeply situated at its proper place, cut it entirely as much as you can, then put moist probes soaked in medicine into quicklime, and push them until they reach the top of the fistula, until the excess left at the bottom is corroded; and then put ointments that invigorate healthy flesh until it be healed; if not healed by this, cauterize as we have said before, and if there are bones corrupted from the fistula, cut them.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the wound or abscess does not bother your main limbs as we have said; and if the bone is exposed with signs of decay and blackening, let it be until the decay is entirely removed, then treat any secondary injuries with ointment until they are healed; and if it is not healed and has become infected again just like before, know that you have not gone deep enough: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all signs of infection, then restore the bone to its place; and if it thus heals, it's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; there are other means to leave it alone naturally; and if there is some small corrupted bone which you can extract with forceps, then remove it with an appropriate tool; and if there are multiple bones affected, take them all out at once, leaving none behind; and if moisture makes this difficult without error or fear, cut away the moisture, flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that causes putrefaction to the wound, and let it rot around the bones until the flesh is more easily separated from them; and if this is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, scrape away only the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; but if much of the matter has been corrupted down to the soft parts of the bone, you must be careful and cut it out entirely up to the limit of corruption, then cure it so that it may heal. And I shall tell you about a fistula which occurred in one man’s leg, from which you can learn an example and help yourself in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause such that matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess without any external reason for opening; but the surgeons in their folly worked on it so much that they opened up the abscess, and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula with many holes through which all kinds of bowels and moisture from his body were emitted. Many doctors treated him as a cure over two years without any expert in surgery until I was called upon; when I saw his leg and medicines they used to treat him, I noted that what came out of the openings was of large bulk; moreover, my patient’s skin turned red and acquired a yellow hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I drove a tent peg into one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming up against the other from every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly rushed and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, with the decay reaching deep inside; I cleaned out what appeared to be the rotten bone, and assumed there was no other decay apart from what I had removed; then I began to restore the wound with soft medicines over a long period, but it would not heal; I started again, and exposed the bone as before, finding that the decay had continued into the bone, so I cleaned it out once more, and then removed it, trying to seal up the hole; yet I was unable to do so even though I cut away an inch of bone around it, revealing its entire core, which turned out to be soft throughout; I restored it with medicines, and it healed swiftly and sealed up promptly, and there was no need to start the procedure again except for the patient's weakness, who could not bear it, and my own fear of death from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation, he often bled, but was completely healed, and in place of the bone, a hard tissue grew, which had good form and caused no harm or discomfort whatsoever, neither when moving nor when resting.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated like this: Take a linen bandage, and stretch it over the head of the exposed bone, and ask someone to pull it upwards; and take another thicker bandage made of wool, and tie it over the flesh above the bone, stretching out the head so that you can move the corrupted tissue underneath, and uncover the area where you want to operate, making sure not to cut or bruise the skin; and place a piece of wood or a spatula under the bone in order to cut away the damaged tissue; and it is necessary to go as deep as one can see and feel the corruption, and then repeat the operation.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or on one side, you must uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron beneath, and with silk or cotton, draw out the corruption from one part to another, and let the suture be of the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and saw through the bone on which it rests on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is nothing else to do but cut them out; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or ankle, this is a very serious matter, nevertheless you must inquire into this corrosion as to how it reveals itself to you; and purify it by all the means possible without injuring the sinew or nerve; and know that there are many instruments for sawing these bones according to their shape, appearance, thickness, subtlety, length, smallness, hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to provide each type of work with its own instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the various diseases; so think about the instrument which is needed.
dou feu	Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head rots either internally or externally; and when you have treated this decay with medicine, and it does not improve, then you must amputate that limb up to the point where the decay begins, so that the patient escapes death, or from the greater evil of losing the entire limb; and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if burnt by fire, and can turn blackish-blue afterwards, because this corrosion spreads from limb to limb, affecting the whole body; act quickly in cutting off the limb, and if it is due to the sting or bite of venomous beasts such as the sea scorpion and snake and their like, if the decay affects the top of the finger, then amputate it and do not allow it to reach further than the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s’elle vient jusc'a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc'a bras; 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs while you operate, cauterize the wound immediately, or apply some restraining powders to it; then return to your medical procedure until it is completed, and bind the affected limb with an appropriate bandage, treating it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man's foot: he had a dark spot that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his toe, spreading throughout his entire foot; when he saw the corrosion, he quickly decided to amputate his foot, but was cured; after a long time, the corrosion returned in his finger, and so he came to me. I applied some counter-irritants after cleansing his body, however, the corrosions did not stop; He requested that I cut off his hand, but I refused because I still had hopes of curing him through counter irritation. I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die since the patient's strength was feeble; The man became desperate and returned to his home where he decided to amputate his own hand, then after doing so, he healed; And let this story be told for others who might need it in the future.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Some time an abscess appears in fleshy places, and remains so long that it creates a great accumulation of pus; then it becomes round and breaks open, and the pus flows out, leaving the flesh bare like some vessels; and the skin that is on top is as thin as delicate fabric, and does not reach down to the bone or nerve; such an illness is called a "sinus", and not a "fistula"; but if it extends all the way to the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula"; and treat this skin by removing that skin entirely around it, especially when it is thin, like some fabric; and do not fear its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear that the skin will rot, and corruption is not deep, but the skin has some flesh attached to it, treat it with a clyster as follows: look to see if the abscess is large, and the pus that comes out of it smells foul; then use Egyptian medicine prepared like this: take equal parts of ash, oil, and litharge, cook them in an earthen vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take according to your need, mix with water and honey, clysterize the abscess, and bind its opening; leave the medicine there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out. Do this many times until the abscess is cleansed of pus. Sometimes you may use a clyster made from ash-water when such medicine is not available. Take ashes of grapewood, pour water over them, let it settle, and use as clyster until you see that the abscess is well cleaned out; and if the patient cannot tolerate this Egyptian medicine or the ash-water, then apply a clyster made from water with honey and just a little bit of litharge ground in it; or one of honey mixed with wine, for honey has properties of cleansing and washing away, while wine causes flesh to rot. And when you have done all this, make sure that the abscess is well cleansed before applying to it some medicated plaster made with rose oil and wine; or apply a clyster with some medicines and ointments whose properties I have discussed in the chapter on ointments. If the opening of the abscess is small and the nozzle of the clyster cannot enter, then you may slightly enlarge it with an iron tool (scalpel), insert into it an Egyptian dressing, or basilicon ointment until its size increases; but if the wound is too large to be sutured closed, just leave a space for the clyster tube to enter through and remove any excess pus that accumulates.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are intact, they do not permit meat to be inserted; and if you cannot cut under them as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the bowel goes to the lowest place where it is, for when the bowel is whole, no flesh can enter there and if you cannot cut below like you want, arrange it this way: let the bowel flow lightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowels; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and spread over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then with force make an incision wider than the first one at the place where the wound is, extend soft ointment according to the size of the wound onto another piece of cloth, apply this onto the wound in order to relieve the bowels, do not remove the larger outer cloth for many days once; and that which is on top of the wound, take it away frequently in order to release the bowel and know what flows from the bowel if its poison or little or enough, or digested, or undigested; and observe whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is abscess or no, when your medicine has been spread out this way and you see the nature that jumps onto the wound, then know that the wound has already healed, and approach the saints. Then untie it in the morning, or on the third day; and as soon as you release the wound, change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast ejects undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle venom takes long to heal, do not despair of the health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people with slow healing of flesh in their wounds, and some who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast takes a long time to heal, and it becomes distant, then apply drying medicines moist in substance but dry in virtue, like refining ointment, for there is much vitriol, which is the final medicine; take refining ointment, made with rose oil, and add equal amounts of old wine; then spread it on and use it; this same mixture works better when cooked and thickened if refining ointment is not available, or you can take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, and sprinkle the powder over honey as it warms up; then glue a cloth to it, apply it over the breast, and sometimes they administer long aristologist needles with roots of celestial lily, which are like flour of fitch and centory; use simple or compound ones: grind them into powder and mix them with the honey I mentioned before, then apply it; and if the cure is prolonged, and does not heal from this treatment, know that corruption has gone deep, causing an impression in bone, or hard tissue, or ligaments; so treat fistula as we have said above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	From the abscess under the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the thumb, or toe, or may arise elsewhere; and when it becomes old, and no attention is paid to it, then a deep-seated abscess appears, and runs and eats away until it reaches the root of the nail, and may eat away the entire nail; and corrosion occurs reaching the bone, causing fetid pain, and the thumb or toe becomes wide, and the color fades.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the classification, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must remove all the excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterizations are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; but if the nail grows into the flesh, begins to pierce it, and makes a wound, then you must put under the nail that presses against the flesh an iron rod which will push it upwards, and scrape off this flesh with care and in a gentle manner, then apply on the remaining part of the flesh caustic or corrosive medicines so as to remove all; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, you must scrape it and trim the flesh, because as long as there is corrupted bone, healing cannot occur; and if you see that the finger is becoming corrupt, then remove the nail from below, just like explained previously, then treat it until it heals; but if it's wounded or bruised and feels severe pain, first proceed with its treatment; afterwards, trim the nail using a sharp spatula by cutting across it, being careful not to reach all the way down to the flesh underneath the nail since this would cause too much pain for the patient; should that happen, apply something soothing on top.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the wrist joint of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two small adjoining fingers that are born in the hands of some men are sometimes very fleshy, and there may be either tendon or bone, and at times they have a nail, and none of them appear in the root of the joint, where their origin is found in various people's hands.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born on the inner side of the finger do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the finger may move; the size of the fleshy one is small, in such a way: cut it off at its root with a wide spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to treat; you must beware of cutting them.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In him who is born or must be at the last night, you must first cut roundly the flesh to the bone, then cut the bone into a fitting piece for it, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sutures that come together in the skull are due to birth, or by joining of a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar causes.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut this suture so that the bones can repair themselves according to their natural forms; then place between them two tents or oily red cloths, moistened, so they do not join again; or you may put between them two pieces of fine lead until the places are united as is proper.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If there are sutures in any of these bones with the palm, then cut this suture as is proper.
des vils	From villages
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Worms are veins greatly swollen filled with melancholy superfluities that come to many body parts; and they occur more often in the legs of those who walk on foot and work hard, than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must therefore administer to him sometimes purging of bile, then the basilic venom.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	Iron treatment is according to two methods: one is when you cut and extract the black blood from bone marrow; and the other method is that you raise the vein and draw all of its blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cut is according to this method: first immerse the leg in very hot water until the large vein is softened, then stretch the patient's leg from above the thigh down past the knee; next make a 1-inch wide incision over the vein at one of three points, lift and draw out the black blood with your hand from end to end, until as much blood has come out as the patient can stand; then tie it off, and instruct him not to eat meat that causes black bile; repeat the evacuation and draining when the veins are full again, which harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatments for this ailment are as follows: remove the patient's leg hair if it is hairy, then place it in a bath and warm the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; if you have no bath, heat it over fire instead, then make an incision above the vein from below the knee to the ankle area; thereafter loosen the skin with a knife, and peel away the flesh on either side of the vein so that it becomes visible when pressed; it will appear red and black, and upon entering the skin it will resemble a white cord; then push the vein beneath, until it is raised from the skin surface; then cut lightly at another point above this with your knife, then loosen the skin around the vein again so it appears; lift the vein as you did before and make an incision in another place 3 inches higher than that; peel away the flesh once more to reveal the vein, then lift up the vein with your finger as you have done previously; cut at a further point above this one, or multiple points if required; lift it again and make an incision at the toe's knuckle; pull and lift until reaching the second incision made earlier; remove it from incision to incision until fully exposed, then make another incision; if unable to pull and lift, insert a needle with strong thread through it and tie up, inserting beneath the vein as well; turn your hand both ways back and forth until it is finished; be careful not to cut for this will hinder pulling or lifting and harm the patient; once fully treated place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil onto the wound site, treat until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the face is distorted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not amputate; and treat it as we mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron with which we cut the face is curved, and does not slice, so that it does not cut the vein; and it has a large curve, for if it were slender, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is engendered in the legs, in warm areas where there are no plants or trees, and on earth that has no moisture; and by chance it may appear elsewhere other than in the legs, and this occurs due to putrefaction which comes from beneath the skin, just as serpents and worms come forth within the body, engendered between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes to the leg, then its color changes, and the vein begins to protrude, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, you must wrap it with a piece of lead that is 3 and a half to 2 inches long, tie it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg. Every time fluid comes out, wrap the lead around it and retie it; if it's too long, cut off a part and wrap the remainder, but do not cut its root so that the entire vein is exposed; for if you cut it, it will retract into the flesh and cause abscesses and putrefaction where it was, resulting in an ill disease. Therefore, it must be treated gradually until the whole thing is gone, leaving no remains on the body. Sometimes this vein, when treated, can measure 5 palms long or 10; a man came to me once whose vein protruded for 10 palms and, upon cutting it, spewed one string of substance and was pierced all the way through so that everything came out; then its matter is evacuated and medicines are brought to fight putrefaction for some days, after which the wound should be treated like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is very delicate, especially when it appears in the ankle joint or foot, and there are many perforations from which blood escapes profusely, so that it must be removed; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that grow between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "ox sickness" in our country because it often occurs in oxen, and it is a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body up and down, and one feels them very well as they travel from limb to limb until they tear the skin where they were and fall out; and they are caused by the corruption of certain humours, just as worms, snakes, and worms in the belly come about; and its malice is doubted, for when it travels through the body and reaches the head, if it goes into the eye, it can destroy it; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and treated, one cannot act except when it appears: so then you must bind the place above and below with a strong tight bond, then cut above and drain it out, and if the poison is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and its greatest harm is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, so tightly bind beneath it the eyebrow, then cut above, and drain it out; and one must use purging of the body with medicine for the bad humours putrid, and beware of foods causing decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land and it's a pain that manifests in certain limbs which can move from limb to limb; I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman and she uncovered her arm revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm; then I saw it rise up like a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it falls from one place to another; the pain left that spot, settled into the shoulder before spreading all over her body eventually reaching the other arm; she told me after this it would go around her whole body as I had witnessed.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly puzzled by how it moved from limb to limb because I had never seen this illness behave in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, but I ne l’avoie want, as com I le vis en la femme; and I me pensai that c’estoit por ceu that li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; and n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	Et when tu vues curer ceste maladie, and li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, and puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; and cauterize le leu; and se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, and semblans others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large points and small, some have hair or are welded; there are those with two angles, and those which have tongues (fletching); and those made in pieces; furthermore they fall into two categories according to the parts of the body that they strike: one type strikes vital organs like the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder etc.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When one of these arrows strikes any of the aforementioned organs and death seems imminent based on the signs which I shall now relate to you: then you must beware extracting said arrow, for many patients will die under such circumstances; but when these evil portents are absent and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then proceed with its removal and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps through the surface that is above the brain, occurs when there is a blackening, burning, turning green or redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and loss of understanding, and vomiting bile; perhaps even discharge of blood from the nostrils or ears; perhaps also losing speech and voice; and appears from the wound white moisture resembling pus, as well as cooked flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then hold back on treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is within.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it falls on the heart are that it is close to the left nipple, and one feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty; perhaps also the pulse changes like the beating of hearts, and there flows out black blood, and comes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrowhead that has not perforated the lung is when there is no foam around the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's colour changes, and they breathe heavily seeking cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls on the covering of the lung, it is close to the small ribs; it causes great pain and great difficulty breathing, and all the limbs from the shoulders are affected.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow hits the stomach, perhaps something undigested from the meat may come out of the wound.
