Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow hits the belly, and no faeces come out through the large intestine, there is little hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows away, and the patient feels intense pain; know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arm and forearm, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, back, waist, thigh, legs, and similar parts, are protected in various ways.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	There was once a man an arrow fell on his shoulder at the base of his neck; I grasped it and pulled it out from beneath the ear's fatty tissue, and he was healed without difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And thrust through the eye into the fat underneath it beneath the paper beneath an arrow whose shaft was of Turk's-turquoise, but we could only get hold of its point towards the stock: and this arrow was all iron light without barbs; the wound was healed, and there befell no evil accident.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian; and this arrow was Arabic with barbs: I watched over its wounds, and extracted it in such a way that I drew out the arrow; and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from a man which was embedded in his belly; and thought that he would die; but after the passing of 30 days, he did not alter from this disposition: I cut above the arrow, and guided it out, and drew forth the arrow without evil accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you have a man with an arrowhead lodged in his back or shoulder, and the wound has healed over; yet the arrow remains inside him, causing no change to its natural position nor any harm to his bodily functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man with an arrowhead in his face, the wound has healed but remains without causing great pain or other significant issues.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treat an arrowhead for the king's man that was lodged in his nose, slightly inclined to the right; the arrow was bent and I was called upon for treatment three days after it had happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	The wound was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it everywhere with a subtle touch, but did not feel it; he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead. I applied a digestive attractive poultice to the place, so that the flesh would not swell; and there appeared to me the flesh of the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for a longer time, and the wound healed immediately, but the patient remained ill for a long period, feeling the arrowhead inside his nose every day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened, and probed, feeling the tip of the arrowhead becoming exposed in the wound; then I adjusted a small hook in the opening of the wound with this medicine until the point of the arrowhead appeared visibly; and the arrow was extracted after four months, and then the wound widened so that I could insert pincers, and I grasped it from one side to another but couldn't remove it; then I didn't cease experimenting and ingeniously devising new instruments, until on one day with well-made pincers, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, I grasped it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The mirror judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	You have told me the quality of extracting some arrows, so that you focus your care on what I do not say, because the book cannot possibly cover everything; but wise masters compare well a little to great things, and for what is present and lacking, invent new work, and new instruments, in order to treat strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not leave the members in which they are stuck for only two reasons: either through the place where they enter, or by another part; and the one that comes out through where it entered is an arrow entering fleshy parts, and this may be the case sometimes.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh is rotten around it, and the outlet is healed; and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, leave it there for a few days, moving it each day; then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a very fine awl until the tissue around it is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the accidents I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the surface, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone, and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains a few days without any ill effects, then devise its extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be extracted directly, then administer probes around it as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged inside the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the wound; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins involved, make an incision until the wound is large enough; draw out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, remove the flesh that is attached to two sides as far as you can, then break or bend the barbs of the arrow so that you may extract it; do this carefully so as not to break the arrow, for doing so would make its removal much more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the surrounding tissues are rotten, then pull it out, for its extraction would be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the loss of blood opposes you, so accommodate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and beware of cutting the nerve and opening a vein, and use whatever means necessary to remove the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how he was positioned when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then lay him down as indicated by the signs.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow has passed through from another side, or nothing appears of it, but the skin is swollen where it can be seen or felt: cut above until the tongs can grasp it, and then extract it; if it leaps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round so that it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone; then draw out the [foreign body].
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be withdrawn, leave it there again and then restart the extraction until it comes out fully; if an arrowhead is stuck in bone, push along the entire shaft of the arrow; if it is embedded and you are administering force to extract it, insert a specially-made instrument with its point entering into the tip of the arrowhead; then push along this device as far as possible, and if the arrowhead has been dislodged, introduce an instrument with its pointed end inwards to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is touching a vital organ, you must cut away all flesh surrounding the poison; if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls onto the foot or thigh or stomach or bladder or side, and it is close by, and you can cut above it, then cut; be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and stitch the wound if necessary; treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to extract arrows is similar to that of a bird's beak, as you can see here: [Image]
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the driving wedge is like that of a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here: [Image]
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pincers for pushing and pulling is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins in the body that can be used for bloodletting, sixteen of which are in the head: two jugulars behind the ears, called 'herbech'; two arteries in the temples; two veins in the corners of the eyes, called 'aspires'; a vein in the middle of the forehead; a vein at the back of the nose; two veins on either side of the neck; two veins above the upper lip, known as 'augeherich'; and two veins underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	There are five veins commonly used for bloodletting in each arm: the cephalic, which is on the left side and is known as the 'head vein' by laypeople; the median, called the 'fast vein', composed of the cephalic and basilica, also referred to as the 'heart vein'; the basilica, located on the right side, known as the 'belly vein' by laymen, found above the elbow, and the one most often used for bloodletting which clearly shows at the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the safety vein is the one that lies between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches; in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is under the curvature of the pocket on the left side, the second one is the sophene at the right ankle; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the other ankle; and in the other leg there are also three veins underneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins behind the ears aids in treating old catarrhs and migraines; and as I told you, the quality of the bleeder is such that you raise the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient tighten his neck with a bandage so that the two veins appear behind the ears at two places dependent on the head: seek them out with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, there make an incision; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein until it reaches bone, then lift your hand all along the length of the vein upwards, and cut both skin and vein quite through with two fingers' breadth, and let out blood as much as you wish; then draw in the edges and bind them up until they are healed; and I have already spoken about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for an old and severe migraine, and for chronic ophthalmia, as well as for the body's production of acute tears in the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeder are as I say: the patient must stretch their neck so that the two veins open clearly; feel the pulse beneath your thumb, then bleed from there; then lift the heart above the vein with your index finger, insert the lancet underneath, and raise the vein, cutting it just as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your needs; then release the patient, put your finger on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top; afterward bind it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; we have already spoken of their incision and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is just as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraine, and redness; and the quality [of the blood] such that the patient strains their neck by twisting it so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called a "digger", whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point of the instrument on the vein and press down with your hand or something else to let blood flow out according to the amount you wish; then release the patient's neck, and bind the wound until it is healed, taking care not to work in too wide a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too pointed and must not strike across [the neck], because of the bone which is close by, and in case it breaks the instrument when being subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two tears helps with the eyes, and for scurfiness, redness, and swelling in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient should twist their neck with some rope, as before; then bleed them, and let the wound be crosswise, a little above the flame, a bit wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the veins are fine, they may break; then make a wound for blood to flow out, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fever, severe headaches, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that appears on the face, especially when it's an old ailment; and the quality of this bleeding is such that the patient should twist their neck and then pinch their nose with your left hand, take a fine long vein, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it heals quickly; and this is the shape of the wound:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of two guindeges helps with the widening of the armpit, the beginning of mastectomy, and many diseases, abscesses, carbuncles, herpes, and tumors; and the quality of the bleeding is such that the patient should tighten their neck under either side, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the patient's head, and let the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein from one long side more widely, then drain the blood gradually or as needed; then repeat similarly in the other vein, then loosen the binding, and gently tighten all veins so that the patient does not strangle; leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cleansing of veins above the lips aids in healing gums and treating gum infections, lip cracks, nose wounds, and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Make the patient sit down facing you and hold their neck firmly as I have explained; then turn back the lip and look at the two veins, one on each side of the upper lip, which can be identified by being darker in colour and surrounded by smaller dark veins: if necessary, open them both up, but first ensure that you know what you are doing. If not, and you are unsure, treat both vessels the same way, as they require identical treatment.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	On the bleeding below the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are beneath the tongue aids after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the eye, and for mouth ailments; and the qualities of the bleeder are such that the patient should sit between your hands facing the sun, lift their tongue, and look underneath on each side for a black vein: bleed one or both, but do not go too deep, as beneath are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by piercing with a wide, blunt lancet, or a sharp, slender olive-shaped one which is called an 'anesil'; they are broad and narrow according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the Martin flame is very renowned, and it is so wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the full veins filled with thick and visible blood, and that contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointedly subtle, and it is for bleeding delicate veins, where there is delicate yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids illnesses that are beneath the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed gently, and to avoid the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it hits the artery, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said; and the wound should not be held but cut like a lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basilic vein does not open visibly, you must draw it out and change to another one; take a little of it, or treat in its place the vein within the arm: it opens visibly; and cut into the wound with a lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of incision, it is necessary that you stretch out the arm and touch the spot until you feel the pulse; then mark this spot with a sign, and bind up the arm, and cut into the wound like a lancet; watch carefully so as not to wound the artery when you see swelling there, for that is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it spurting upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore hasten and press your finger upon it for some time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, as often happens; bind his arm, and leave it thus, and do not move him, patient; and fear may come, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and he faints, and no medical professional is present, then sever the artery if it is visible, for this will stop him from suffering; and stanch the blood flow.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fustic bark, split it, and take one half, binding it well until the next day; if the bleeding is stopped, that is good; if not, then treat him as we have said, with blood-stanching powders; and this stanching is not grievous in many cases due to the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The opening of the vein in the middle helps as it draws blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the surgeon must watch out for the nerve that lies beneath, and if he pierces too deeply there, and he finds the nerve, and it swells up and the wound becomes infected, then perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, but if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, you must treat it with a gentle instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make an incision along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The opening of the cephalic vein is helpful as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one must treat it by making an incision with an olive-oil flame or a myrtle-oil flame, for this is the safest method for all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to seek the lightest position, and not to do any harm if one fails the first time, and one starts again; and by chance some men's limbs may swell when they fail the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the discharge is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that bleeding is not done except to preserve health and avoid future illnesses; and let the bloodletting be performed in one of three veins which are: namely, the cephalic vein, the median cubital vein, or the basilic vein; and it should be carried out at the beginning of Lent while fasting, and during autumn and winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; and it should take place on the first day or third, two or three hours after the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding administered for illnesses has no determined time, but rather when the need arises day or night, at all hours and in every season; and it is not advisable to bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a woman carrying a child before four months have passed up until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They should not bleed the elderly who have exceeded sixty years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be bled, regardless of the method, they should first cleanse their intestines with a light clyster if there is an excess of feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out harmful waste from the intestines and damage the principal organs; one should also avoid bleeding those who are overly full from meat, drunk, or suffering from dropsy. Be wary of bleeding after episodes such as colic, vomiting, belly pains, frequent sexual intercourse in women, labor, lack of sleep, fasting, or any kind of hardship involving the body or mind; then purify the humors if the blood is thick due to excessive consumption of food and drink, or from medicines, provided you are able. Then enter the bath, unless there is something preventing this, as a way to thin out the blood, and bleed from the vein on the arm's underside, nearest the elbow, as we have mentioned; avoid exertion that day, refrain from labor, strain, sexual activity, or any similar activities; stay calm and happy, with the bleeder positioned higher than the one being bled, and rub the patient's arm twice or three times before tying off the vein firmly but not too tight, for this could prevent the blood from flowing. Then massage the area with your hands until you can feel the veins bulging beneath them; then dampen the wound with a small amount of old oil, place your left thumb on the chosen vein directly below where it is to be opened so that the vein does not break when cut, and avoid any twisting or bending at this spot.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that bleed like ropes in a butcher's shop, and some are full of windiness such that when you apply the flame it retreats from the flame, and one cannot open the vein; thus it is with these people; if one opens the wound then the injury is too small, therefore one must be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened on the first attempt, it is good; but if not, try again a little below or above that spot, unless the area is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the area is swollen and the patient becomes alarmed, leave it for one or two days, do not bind their arm: perhaps a hot abscess will develop; do not go in the bath, then try again with cauterization if you wish; and if the opening is small, let the blood flow gently out and if you doubt that enough blood has come from this spot, apply the flame directly to it; work a little above or below instead of where the vein is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, and apply a poultice of oil, for it lightens the body from blood, and the oil is beneficial in this place; thus administer the oil poultice to every wound that treats veins, to staunch the flow of blood; and likewise does triacle and bowels, when applied on the site, act subtlety to draw out excess blood and separate it if too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there is a large abscess that occurs frequently, especially when it has not been cleaned except for the time of opening the wound or vein, then hurry and apply to the place a sponge moistened with warm water and salt, constricting it for an hour; you must do this after the blood has drained from the wound, and if there remains at the site after some days a blackness or greenness, it will not harm; and should you see this, apply something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in wormwood juice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	For there often occurs an abscess and appearance at the wound of the basilica: so put your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, this is that evil appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Refrain then from putting anything upon it of what we have said, for perhaps there is a court without the artery; but do this: apply a dry poultice to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the colour of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it come out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and robust, and requires blood extraction, that a wider wound be made, and the flames should be broad; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is advisable to bleed them little and often, and one must bleed them by making a diagonal cut, not a deep one; and this manner of bleeding is safe from excessive blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is necessary to give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are heated, draw three or four times from the blood; and if they are of a cold complexion, eat moistened bread in muslin syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the procedure after a lot of blood has been let out, it is necessary for him to drink meat broth and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to vent his arm and bleed again, when he is weakened by excessive bleeding, it is necessary that he bleeds little by little, according to the amount of strength he has continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wishes to vent his arm after the first bleeding and has strong constitution, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wishes to bleed in another place, he should be bled on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has much blood inside the body which is already heated, and causes fever; you must draw out a large quantity, and enlarge the opening until it stops by itself; then attend to all conditions of healing, and put your hand on their pulse as they heal, so death does not come instead of relief, and this happens many times when healers are negligent; and do not do this when you want to release the arm, and cause blood to flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly upon it; or if it is crooked, that he extends his arm quickly, for this would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or put a point at the tip of the flame, so the congealed blood from the vein's opening flows out, and put on some salt soaked in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain blood a second time, let the vein be opened in that same place or in another wound or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arm is opened in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The way of opening the vein is such that the patient places their hand in warm water until the veins are red; then they should be tied loosely so the vein appears clearly, and now open it across, not from side to side or lengthwise; the hole should be wide and the incision made close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, place the hand back into warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; but if this is done in winter, do not put their hand back into warm water again because we do it more often in winter than summer; and the opening of this vein is safer than any other veins, whether artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the saviour of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: extend the hand, and dip it in warm water until the vein swells, so that it can be seen; and if the bleeding occurs across the vein, and you cut it from one end to another, it will not cause harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are all exposed underneath without flesh, and then put the hand back into warm water, if the blood has frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn out as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and linen to the vein to weld together the wound, and do likewise for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding of the one on the left hand is beneficial for illness of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The draining of the spleen is beneficial for all diseases that are below the body, such as diseases of the uterus, retention of urine, kidney ailments, and similar conditions in the thighs and old legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its drainage is such that the patient immerses their foot in hot water and rubs over the vein until it perishes, then bind above the ankle joint; and this vein lies at the ankle, extending up along the leg towards the kidneys; drain either the larger kidney or where it appears best to you.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it over the foot, be cautious of the nerves that run beneath, and drain gently across them as when cutting; let the flame be small.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot exit, return the foot to the water, and allow the vein to be properly emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incision fails the first time, begin again a little higher up, for the skin is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and proceed in the same manner on the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is located at the base of the heel, and its incision helps with hip pain when it involves hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of this incision is such that the patient must enter the bath and have their heel tightly squeezed for four days while twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, treat it in every way possible, including transversely; and be aware that you may need to cauterize it, because the skin is salty, and it is very responsive to touch in most men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't find it, cauterize any line of it that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful not to hit the nerves; make the blood flow as much as you can see, then untie the ligature, and apply cotton and press; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	bloodletting with cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping instruments are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping without wounding is also done in two ways: either with heat or without heat; and the cupping that involves wounding and blood extraction is performed on fourteen places of the body, some being right at the top of the head; others are in the middle of the neck; two more are on the sides of the neck; one under the chin; two on the shoulders; two on the hips; two on each arm; two on each leg; and finally two on each ankle. Cupping draws out only a small amount of blood from numerous tiny veins spread throughout the flesh, and does not weaken you in any way like vein-letting does. It should never be administered, whether with or without heat, for any illness caused by overabundance as it empties all the body's humours.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if due to the necessity of illness suction cups must be applied, or for treatment, let's administer them each hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and in between as well; because there are some who when they need cupping have a heavy head; and others find fullness and redness on their face, and on their neck, darkening around the eyes; and some see drops of blood in their mouth, with swollen tongues and bleeding gums; and there are those who experience dreams and visions of blood, wounds, death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially during the middle of the month, we instruct them to be cupped after every three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with inflammation ... that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after evacuating all the body's blood; this venesection is in place of the bleeding from the head, and it should not be used by those of a cold constitution or who have catarrh, as it causes them great harm; therefore, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently bleed become forgetful, so the cup should be placed slightly lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	Venesection in the middle of the neck is in place of bleeding from the head and basilic vein, and because of this it is useful for narrowing of the oesophagus, and ruptures in the stomach lining, and vomiting, and fullness; and one should not push too hard, as if it holds too firmly, it causes forgetfulness or affects the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilations on the two collarbones are useful for headaches, eye inflammation, migraine, and strangulation; they also treat pain at the roots of teeth and can be used in place of a basilic incision; you must instruct the surgeon to guide their hand carefully so as not to cut the artery nor cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	Ventilations below the chin are useful for mouth diseases and gum infections as well as similar conditions in the mouth; they can be used instead of incisions on both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations over the shoulders treat conditions caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	Ventilations on the armpits are as useful as incisions on three veins of the arm because they draw blood from these large veins; instruct the surgeon not to cut too deep as there is no flesh in that place only nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is on the buttocks is useful for haemorrhoids of the anus and diseases underneath, and it should be large, made of copper as it needs to suck well; and perhaps if it were thin, it would break; and it causes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs clearly heal, as they attract blood from all over the body, and are useful for old pains of the kidneys, uterus, and bladder, and restore menstruation; and they go in place of two sophenes, or two ankles, but still they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting fits in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you put it on first when empty, suck in temperately, and apply quickly, moving evenly, and do not cease until you see the place red and swollen, and the redness of blood appears; then stop, and replace the cups, being mindful of the body's condition, for there are those who have tough flesh, or clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and make broad wounds, a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very dense, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out a little at a time, we are satisfied with just one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to take out a great amount of blood, we start often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply and fully, so that the heart is suddenly pierced, and it is necessary for him who has coarse skin and hard, whose pores are narrow, that you grease the cups with an aperitif and dissolving oil: if in summer, violet oil, or almond oil, or gourd seed oil; and if in winter, cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess [material] is large and cold, take marjoram oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and their likes.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being treated has tender flesh and wide pores, it is not necessary to apply oil, but rather wash it after ventilation with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry juice, or squash juice, or china root juice, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excessive moisture, rise easily with myrtle water, or sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with large excess [material], rise from old wine, or liquorice water, or aniseed decoction, or chamomile, or others like it; and they should not be treated with cupping before the bath nor in a bath, but after the bath by one or two hours; and do not sleep after the ventilation, and must keep warm when being cupped and afterwards.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care if the patient is choleric, and their blood is too sharp and inflamed; they should eat cold things, such as pomegranates, endive, lettuce in vinegar, similar foods; also mint juice, pork fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold complexion, give them honey syrup and aromatic medium wine, which is between old and new, eat little pork, mint juice, small birds, and pigeons; on the day they are cupped, they should drink more than eat; sometimes give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping to strengthen their main limbs; let the blood be thin, but those who are hot must not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are applied without injury are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, podagra, and on the abdomen, hips, and kidneys; for these organs do not tolerate wounding in any way, and it is only to attract blood from one part of the body to another, just as we place them on the breasts when the infant suckles; to remove the viscosity that exists in an organ, which we achieve by placing cups on the abdomen and hips so as to reduce its size; and also alleviate pain where there is an obstruction or a stone, perhaps removing the obstruction due to its attractive virtue, or displacing the stone from its place; it acts in this way when placed upon the liver and spleen if there is retained windiness, and these cups are applied empty for suction alone; they may sometimes be filled with warm water mixed with fire, and other times simply with tepid water as is done for pleurisy; we fill the cup thusly using only warm water, or with some herbs which have been boiled in water.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The procedure of cupping using fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches in width and half a palm lengthwise, with a small hole at the side near its center, just large enough for inserting a needle, and it is made of brass, soft in front so as not to hurt the patient when applying on the limb; and in the middle there should be a bar across of either brass or iron, for placing a burning candle, and they come in various sizes depending on the ailments and ages of those who use them; because cups used on children are different from adults, and thin people require other sizes than fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	To use this cupping device, one must proceed in the following manner: take a wax candle or an oil lamp and insert it into the cup through the bar that is inside of it, so that its flame lies at the bottom of the cup without burning the patient; then apply the cup to the limb, with your fingers covering the hole we mentioned earlier, such that when you want to release vapor, remove your fingers from said hole and take off the cup; proceed in this manner using oil lamp as described before, repeating often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure used to treat pleurisy, it is entirely hollow and has no nozzle or opening. It is applied only when filled with water and placed directly onto the affected limb.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cupping is not applied to areas where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, or similar parts; nor to any uncovered flesh like the tongue or nails, and other comparable places. The quality of using them lies in finding cupping glasses that are filled with clear, clean water without dirt, taking them, placing one overnight into pure water until they become familiarized and have nothing inside their interior. Then you must bleed from both vein and cup, afterwards rubbing the limb until it is red, then place the cups on top; once they are full, remove them if this is a spot where cups can be placed as it will greatly benefit later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, lift the wound slightly, then with water, very well, and then press it; if the wound heals too much after the flesh, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it on top until the blood is staunched; if the blood is excessive, apply powdered vitriol or gallstones, and similar things, until it stops flowing; you can put half of some peeled beans on the wound and leave them there for as long as they are warm against the wound to staunch it now; and if more is required, take other flesh.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the flesh does not want to be taken, rub the wound with fresh blood or stick a needle into it until blood comes out and then put them on top; as soon as they feel the blood, they will warm up; when you see that they are falling off, sprinkle some powdered aloes and boiled ash over it so they will now fall.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	My dear son, know that the foolish surgeon who ignores this chapter will never see any of the ancient medical books, nor read their letters; and for this reason, science is foreign in our land, as I have never found a good one; I have no knowledge other than through the wisdom of these ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated patients with it, by experience, and by my own practice over time; I have described to you in this chapter what is contained within, abbreviated at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.
