It is necessary, therefore, that we say in the prologue of this book the main points of what has been said and which chapters the wise man set forth his intentions, and remains true to reality, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When a fracture or dislocation or torsion or rupture occurs in someone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on one side and then the other, unless something prevents it like frailty of body, childhood, or old age; or if the weather is very hot or too cold; avoid eating cold foods such as raw vegetables and goat meat, do not drink wine or eat fatty meats, nor over-indulge in meat that fills veins with blood until you are sure there's no risk of a warm abscess forming or an outbreak of matter at the affected limb. In this way may the patient return to their previous state of being before injury.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that produce thick nourishment or are viscous, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and calf's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this thick nourishment helps the healing process and speeds up the recovery from the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones in the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as small children; but do not despair, apply over the broken bone large splints which bind and join the limb together, until it regains its strength as before; do not leave them there for long, and therefore they must be nourished with fatty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that dislocations are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the spine, or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	As there is fracture that requires sawing, and another by sharpening, like cutting the tip of a quill to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is fracture with an open wound, or fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type there is its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory returns to its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by that which is twisted out of place, appearing clearly on the surface, sounding hollow when pressed with the hand; and where there is no twist nor a sound to touch, and the patient feels little pain, then it is not a fracture but rather dislocation or fissure.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but apply the medicine that follows hereafter, then hold it firmly and gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes into bone, where the two parts are separated, they must now be brought together evenly, otherwise a cold abscess will form there; and if a cold abscess forms, leave it alone for one day until the abscess subsides; then reset it smoothly and gently, and know that the healing of this type of break is quicker than those with pieces; then hold it as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces broken in the bone, separate it into two parts, whether hand or foot, or take your own hand if it is a small limb, or use two cords, or one cord and your hand; set the member according to its natural shape so that when the fractured part of the member is disjointed, bring together by all means its edges as best you can without causing injury or pain to the patient; align well the ends of the bones in accordance with their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you will feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well: handle it gently and do not restrain it too much or press it so tightly as those who through their work bring hot abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, chastise well the patient so that they do not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, or during any other movement; make sure the limb is secure and that there is no pain felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain felt, it is not yet in place, and you must put it into such a position that there is no pain; be careful to ensure it is properly aligned so that it does not become crooked once reset; the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in smallness, largeness, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs like arms and fingers, wrap soft and fine linen cloths; for larger ones such as thighs and legs, use wide, sturdy bandages, as these embrace the entire large limb, constricting it equally on all sides so there is no pressure. Then bind with light pads, three or four turns according to the limb's size, tightening your hand slightly around the bandage. Go above the break and tighten less where the fracture can shift away from; loosen the bandage gradually until you reach a significant part of healthy tissue. Repeat this process with another bandage, returning to the broken area, binding moderately neither too tight nor too loose as mentioned before. Place linen pads or cloths between the bandages evenly then bind everything above with a tourniquet and finally apply your splints if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply a soothing poultice to reduce the abscess and alleviate swelling, leaving it on for several days; then place upon your stars, which are made of half of a wide cane cut lengthwise into strips, or from the wood used for cleavers, or palm branches, fashioned thusly:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the star you place on a fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others; it should also be as long as appropriate for the size of the limb, small or large; then fasten upon the stars as you did with the first bandage, then bind above with thread appropriately, as in the first bandage used for fractures; being narrower on top, and broader below; and the thread must be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the thread is coarse, like I have seen from the work of fools who make their ligatures with twisted linen cord, this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than two fingers' breadth between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the bones of the stars after their veins are constricted, place pads made of linen or woolen cloth underneath to prevent any injury.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a fracture and the heart is broken, I shall discuss its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not suitable to extract bones from all fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, one should not insert bones before five or seven days have passed, or more depending on the severity of the abscess and its symptoms; here I will show you the ancient method of plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and torsion: take some flour from the inner walls of a millstone, mix it with plenty of eggs, then apply this mixture, neither too runny nor too thick, making sure to use it, for this is how most people treat broken bones in various circumstances, especially women and small children, as it is neither overly harsh nor cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Autre maniere d'emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d'uef; se li complexion de l'ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Autre maniere d'emplaustre que vaut a torsion: take mugwort and viscum albus, each 10 zettalitres; myrrh and aloe, each nine zettalitres; acacia six zettalitres; Armenian bole ten zettalitres, and grind well, then mix with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of emplaster for joints and dislocated bones, to ease the pain arising from wear on the bone, and fractures: take new wool, soak it in warm oil then cook it in oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This emplaster does not restore, but it is good to ease hot abscesses, and properly removes pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of a plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-softened clay leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of a plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to reduce the remnants of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take roots of marshmallow, chamomile flowers, violet flowers, vetch flour, each in equal parts; grind them together and mix with wine; if the limb is hot, mix with moist coriander water or plain water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of a stronger plaster than the first one for when a hard abscess comes to restoring the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that one should not apply anything to the broken limb to restore it other than a mixture of wax and oil, nor any other substance more, and he states that this should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one must apply dry substances, slightly warm, onto the broken limb for restoration, such as myrrh and aloe, incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of plaster that is good for pain and injury: take mugwort and human hairs chopped up, or feathers from birds, and common mallow, and mix them equally, then grind them to make a plaster, adding glue.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then undo the binding a little later and be sure that the patient does not feel any pain or that the bone has moved out of place; do not unbind it too soon by hand, And if the pain returns to this spot, or itching, or there is restlessness or swelling, then hurry up and undo it now, and take light cloth, and sea sponge moistened, dip in water and apply to this area until the itch stops and the pain calms down; leave the limb at rest for an hour, then place dry wool soaked either in water or rose oil over it, and bind again but not as tight as before, carefully until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has been completely removed, with no redness, pain, or swelling left behind, and you need to apply a plaster cast and bandages, start over again just as you did previously and evenly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb doesn't respond to any of what we've discussed, you shouldn't attempt to release it until after three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes even leave it alone for twenty days, as experience shows, until the fracture is healed and the flesh has drawn near again; then restrain it more firmly than before, and thicken its flesh, just as I mentioned earlier; and if you see that the place dries out beyond what's necessary, know that nourishment can't reach there anymore; pour warm water on it every time you release it, each third day, and loosen up a little. Through this process, then, nourishment will return to the limb, correcting the deformity caused by those foolish doctors who restore the limb incorrectly: which is bad, and very dangerous practice too, as I see no alternative but to leave it alone and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures and various forms, and the causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the point pierces through all the bone down to the soft part beneath the bone, as an axe or a stick does; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called 'axed'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'absolute'; and these two types of fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or splitting, or the point of a stone, or falling on stones, or similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing break that reaches up to the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that pierces the bone as subtle as a hair, and it has a small crack, therefore this break is called 'capillary'; and if the wound is made by striking stone, or falling, or similar, and causes a piece of bone to enter inwardly, with its edges like those made by a blacksmith when forging cauldrons; so too does the stone go inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those with moist bones in the head, like infants; and it occurs for all these types of breaks that small fragments are detached like stars; I will speak of them at the appropriate time.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of fractures through their dislocation, examination at the tents, and corrupted flesh that is above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is recognized by this: when the bone has been exposed and you rub over it, the black fracture opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take care of the patient's accidents and complications; if you see no ill accident such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, fainting, ague fever, eyes going out red, or other similar things in many different dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no fearful accident and hope for recovery, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes to you first, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the membrane beneath the bone be corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture reaches up to the membrane covering the brain, you must split the affected area like this: take hold of the wounded person's head and uncover over the bone in every way possible, especially above the wound; should bleeding occur when uncovering the bone or abscess forms, apply the appropriate aid, filling the space with moistened rags soaked in rose oil; let it rest until the hot abscess is soothed and you are sure there is no more blood loss; then begin around the bone to remove it, which must be done according to two methods of work: one method involves cutting a narrow incision in front, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another incision greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, made of hard iron; work them gently so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, you must bore around it rather than administering incisions with trepans that are not completely perfect so as not to perforate beyond the skull bone, and it should have a margin or circle above the point, which prevents the point from passing through the bone; you need several of these so that each comes into place in accordance with the species of bone, thus having trepans for all skulls; this is how the three types of trepans are formed:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities required to pierce around the broken bone are that you place the auger on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the auger elsewhere a little further away, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the perforations with the incision tools, doing so as finely and gently as possible, as we have said, until you can remove the bone by hand or with any instrument such as pincers, tongs; and be careful not to touch the brain or membranes.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is necessary that you use an appropriate tool to scrape off any remaining debris from the bone using another instrument similar to an incision tool but finer and more delicate; if there are small bones or scales left over, gently remove them with the tools; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen describes, which is more safe; and he praises it strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears, so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place underneath the head of this lens-shaped cutter, for which there is this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, as the cutting edge is sharp on both sides, so that the blades face towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet above, so that you chip away at the bone all around, and take care of the membrane that lies underneath; if it sticks to the bone, remove it lightly, for it can be removed easily without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the marrow, and the bone is merely sliced above it, with small pieces present, you must remove this roughness, and use a subtle scraper with various quantities of blades that you should possess, to adjust for each place the most suitable one, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large scrapers first, then finer ones afterwards, and do not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate fractures and hairline cracks, you must adjust their causes according to its direction; this is something that cannot be answered by anyone who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the wound is exposed, you must take a piece of linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, placing it onto the wound; then take another piece of cloth, doubled over twice or three times, dampen it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; do this lightly so as not to aggravate the wound, then apply another binding above, but do not tighten it too much that it causes pain; leave it there for one or two days until the hot abscess has calmed down, then remove it, and apply internal medicine such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, and similar substances; make a powder from these things, and put it on the wound, then apply external medicines without any biting qualities; ensure that the wound remains clean, do not allow pus to build up or for scabs to form, because when scabs appear over the membrane of the brain, they will run and rot, causing great harm to the patient; whenever you place something biting onto a wound, it will necrotize above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any mishap befalls the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no discoloration except for the medicine that has been applied, with such effect, you must take a portion of honey, and three parts rose oil and glue one dressing, applying it to the wound; then treat it in the manner of treatments necessary until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the upper arm are broken, or just one, for there are two bones; and the lower bone is cartilaginous, it does not break but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the hollow of the arm and place that break evenly within your index finger, and push from the outside until the arm returns to its natural shape; do this gently, taking care not to cause pain in the patient through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is above the nose, and the bones cannot be brought together, you must set it equal to the head of a slightly thicker nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is in two places, make another one like it, and hasten to restore the first on the same day, if you can; if not, after seven or ten days, when the hot abscess has cooled, then place some thin linen cloth at the head of the nose, if the fracture is in a single part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you place the other one elsewhere if there is a fracture there; and let these cloth tents be so thick that they fill the nose's openings.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one should wet the tents with butter, and change them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but they should be moistened in a preparation of egg white and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bones are firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are pushed into the wound instead of tents, and if you have soft cloth, wrap it around, and hold the break, and blow through the patient's nose; do as seems best to you.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess appears in the nose while you are working on it, apply a piece of waxed cloth or some cotton moistened with rose oil, or dip it in diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no abscess appears there, apply an external plaster made of flax seed flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then cover it with light toweling and do not bind the nose; and if the break in the nose is small, and it has broken into tiny pieces, remove these with suitable instruments, then clean the wound thoroughly and treat any foreign matter left inside like iron, soldering them together as with plasters and ointments appropriate to this; and if there are no wounds inside the nose, then treat it with tents and insert canes of lead until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of a broken jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken from below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only outside, not split into two, nor bent inward, it can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left jawbone, use the index finger of your right hand to push the fracture inward gently, then align it with the other hand from outside, making sure it is even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is split into two pieces, you must apply traction to both parts until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement or fracture of the teeth occurs, restrain them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply cerate to the broken jaw and place over it two cloths; put on these cloths a large splint well made, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and bind this all together as best you can, commanding the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, release them on the third day, and then reset what has changed; apply a plaster over it with mill powder and an abundance of egg or sisam flour after removing the cerate; put light woolen cloth over the plaster, and should the plaster harden but there is no change in the patient's condition, leave it until they are healed; often this healing takes three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess arises, bring about what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break with an accompanying wound, remove no part of the bone if it has been taken out; extract it gently using suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with a flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, sew the wound shut if it is wide; apply suitable plasters over it to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	Of hernia.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Hernia breaks many times in front towards the shoulder and the break is of three kinds: it is broken and torn into two with parts missing which is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture accompanied by a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is thus when there is a fracture without injury, have two assistants such that one holds the shoulder which feels the fracture force; and the other extends his neck towards the affected area; then equalize the fracture with your two hands so that its form is as it should be, nor does it exhibit appearance or completion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to further extend it, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, its size according to your needs; stretch and lift the fracture force, and press the sphere with your hand so that you equalize the fracture as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the fracture out due to it being too deep, have the patient lie often on their harness and place a medium-sized pillow under their shoulder; push the ministers' shoulders down so that the bone of the fracture is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you find it splintered, you must cut above it; draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, then chop it with one of the incising instruments that you have; but put some force behind this instrument to prevent further damage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It should be shaped like a spoon, and is not sharp, but rather broad, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the wound; it has two ends, as you can see, one wide and the other narrow, like the shape of the wound that was made when you drew out the bones; once you are certain of hot abscesses, cut open the wound if the rupture is small or suspect a hot abscess, then fill up the wound with lint and tented gauze, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess appears, moisten a cloth with rose oil, olive oil, and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Bind the broken bone, when it is wounded and splintered, by applying an ointment made from mill dust and egg white, then place light dressings on top, and put a stick under the armpit if needed; take a very wide bandage one palm in width, then double-layer the cloth over the dressing, and apply the ointment; take a thin strip three fingers thick and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that its end hangs down; place the strip onto the fracture, and tie the bandage around the neck and under both armpits; draw each part of the binding together, and when you see that it holds the break properly, and clearly see that the strip doesn't move from above the broken bone, bind it tighter daily as needed; make the patient lie on their back, and give them a small pillow under the armpit when sleeping to lift the shoulder upwards; this lessens the stress of the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck if you see ill accident may come, for twenty days; then reapply the ointment as needed, tighten it again, and leave it like that until they are healed; it will heal in at most twenty-eight days, but sooner with some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For a shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Until the shoulder is set in its place, either high or low, and not moved by touch; align it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it following its natural form as best you can; then apply some flour-powder with egg white, soft wadding, and a double cloth; on top of that add a wide, thin splint slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are any strands from the splint below the arm, fill those areas in with linen swabs so that the splint sits evenly; then firmly bind it all up with a large bandage so the splint does not move from its place, and check the bindings each day; every time they loosen, retighten them, and adjust the splint if it has moved out of place, laying the patient on their side; after 20 or 25 days the shoulder will be healed, and once these numbers are reached you may remove the bandages, being sure as bone does not mend so lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a fragment of the bone sticks out before and pierces beneath the heart, make an incision above it, remove it, and do as we have said for calming the hot abscess in the breakage of the collarbone.
de la brisure dou pis	From the fracture of the hip.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The hip is sometimes fractured in two, but this occurs rarely; it often breaks outwardly.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in two, it slants downwards and the patient experiences great pain, lacks mobility, becomes bedridden, perhaps vomits blood, and the ends of the broken bone protrude through the skin, which is easily verified.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is such that the patient lies frequently on their back, and a cushion is placed between their shoulder blades; then press the shoulder blades together and bring the sides of the two sets of ribs close to each other with your hands, doing this carefully so that the shape of the bone may be restored as it should; afterwards apply dressings and lay fine gauze soaked in salt water or another light substance on top, wrapping it all in a cloth and tying it securely to the broken bone such that there is no movement; then tie bandages around the back in circular fashion, tightening them suitably, and release their tension every hour, tightening again if they have slackened; and should it be necessary to loosen them due to corrosion or itching of the area, pain, or abscesses, do so quickly, removing the dressings, cleaning away any matter that has accumulated there according to methods for treating wounds, then redress the wound and tighten the bandages until healing is complete.
de la brisure des costes	De the breaking of ribs.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of ribs only comes from their large size after the back, and to the head within, and they do not bend except for those which are brittle; and one feels it well upon examination by touch.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the break evenly, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a plaster, and bind it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib break is directed inward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, like pricking, because the bone pierces the lung; and immediately upon breathing, they cough and spit up large clots of blood, it is an urgent matter, and the ancients have used great appliances for this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And so there are some who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to expel the rupture outwardly.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not cause it, for hot abscesses to come, if they have not already arrived.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have arrived, then treat them with cauterization.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say that we should apply cups to the site, in order to draw out the humors forcefully, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cup may attract superfluities back to the site due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that we should cover the site with moist wool in hot oil, and apply tents between the ribs to level out the surrounding flesh, then let it be treated by the treatment for pleurisy, of diet and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pressing on the flesh, and there is doubt about their condition, then it is necessary to make an incision over the location of the broken rib, and one must place a tool underneath to protect the lung; thereafter, one must cut into the bone, extract gently, and then sew the two lips of the wound together if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a warm abscess arises, apply damp cloths soaked in rose oil onto the affected area, and place them there; treat the site with what is appropriate for an abscess, and ensure it lies frequently on its side where necessary until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	On the fracture of the neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is breakage of bones in the neck, which often leads to bending; this also occurs in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you wish to know if they will heal or not, take note: if their hands are softened, swollen, and deadened, unable to move or extend; and when pricked with a needle, they feel no pain.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many cases, and if they change and feel better when the joints are moved and prodded, know that the bone's socket is safe, and the patient will be cured with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know if they will heal or not: take note if their feet are softened, and if there is any accident involving their hands, as well as wind and involuntary voiding on the back; and when they are turned onto their stomach, there should be involuntary voiding.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and wishes to sit down, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal; do not delay in treating it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, the matter is more trivial.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is as follows: if there is hot inflammation, apply oil of roses or fresh yolk of egg until it is calmed; then place a comforting and drying poultice, bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is severed, you must cut above the heart; remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment to encourage flesh growth until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken off, which is called 'the head of the cow', insert your thumb from your left hand, and align it evenly with your other hand's strength, then apply a poultice and splint if necessary; then hold it firmly, and if there is any dislodged bone, do this again, removing it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hip bone is broken, there will be only a little reduction at the head, and it fractures down its length, deviating towards the opposite side, causing pain in that spot for the patient, as well as tenderness and swelling where it was fractured.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above it, so that you are over the break; and know where the fracture is and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, make sure this fracture is even, such that it regains its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is down its length, or it deviates inwards, make the patient lie on their belly so that you can see the restoration of this fracture.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it evenly, apply the plaster, then place a wooden or metal rod above it, and compress the fracture so that it does not move; support this area under the armpit until the ligament is aligned.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if a hot abscess forms there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has cooled down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the restoration process, holding [the wound] as required, unless any unfavorable event occurs; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	On fracture of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires are those bones located between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if they are broken, you must restore them according to one of two methods. The first is that you take a wooden stick of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the stick to each side of the patient's broken arm, and lift it up. Then place the patient on a chair; then lay their broken arm on the stick, until it reaches the armpit, and have half a bend of wood placed in the middle of the stick, then let them hold something heavy or let an assistant stretch their arm downwards; finally put their hands together at the point of breakage so that the break realigns properly.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to let the patient lie on their back with their neck tied to one hand; then command two assistants: one should hold what's above the break at his hands and the other should support underneath the entire arm and stretch it downwards so that they both pull in opposite directions from each side of the break.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then bind the cord below the fracture, and above it as well, and have each of the assistants pull on their respective ends.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you must place a cord halfway below the armpit, and another towards the front, below the fracture; likewise, if the fracture is towards the front, the cord should be placed lightly without strain so that the fracture is aligned in the joint and on the front side; then align the break as required, and bind it, unless an abscess forms.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess forms, do not bind it for seven days, and place a moist dressing made of easy and red rose oil on it until the abscess is eased; then bind it, but take care to place the plaster over the fracture first, then assemble the arm onto the splint, and put your hand over the shoulder or chest; wrap the cloth around and bind it firmly over the splint and arm so that the arm stays in position without moving, unless something hinders this, or if the bone has shifted.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint over the break, leaving two inches of space between each one; each splint should extend three inches beyond either side of the fracture; then pull on the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter regarding fractures, more strongly but less frequently.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see that the splints are in place and tightened as we have said when you restore the broken limb, and you suspect a hot abscess, let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have mentioned; then check every three days to ensure no itching or swelling occurs at the site, nor any necrosis of the limb due to excessive tightness.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, do not release him from this position unless after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach; place a cushion filled with wool evenly underneath the injured area, and watch every hour during the day or night that the broken limb does not move nor the ligaments soften; if he recovers by virtue of medicine, feed him the diet we mentioned earlier, in such a way that at first the food is delicate; and as he begins to recover, let it be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the injured area and leg should be reexamined after forty days in total, at which point he must be released from this position and given a bath with medicated oils to realign his joints.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is severe and stuck, it may take a day or two months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	From the breaking of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the 'humerus', with one being smaller, attaching to the wrist, and the other larger, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large bone breaks, or maybe the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bone is broken, it heals quickly and easily; but when the large bone is fractured, recovery is slower and more difficult than if both were broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, it should be lightly extended and made even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large fossa, you must compress more strongly; extend him on the cushion, and hold the wrist of his hand higher than the others, and his little finger lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their legs over themselves, and the cushion in front of them higher, so that the patient does not suffer any strain; then stretch the ministers' arms to the part below his hand or cord, and another minister above him.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place equal mirrors for him, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, set each one in its place, and if any piece is detached from the heart and you cannot restore it to its place, then bend and remove it as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with broken bones at the wound, as I have spoken of it in a separate chapter; then take its cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration, warm abscesses appear, use a plaster made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; bind the cloth gently above it so that the warm abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the plaster, and apply an ointment made from mill dust with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint of the broken bone be closer to stronger and a little wider than the others; know that there must be six splints or arms in various arrangements: whether the break is in one bone or two; bind more tightly above the break than elsewhere, and always less so as you move away, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; let the cloths which are placed on the break be soft and moist, but not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And support the member and its ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident occurs in the member, such as itching that arises in the member, then it is necessary for you to sprinkle the member with warm water until these itches are soothed; and let the member not be too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the tightening, and if the ligament is softened and the bones disjointed, or a similar case, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like this for a few days until circulation reaches it, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said bring relief to the patient, do not release him for twenty days.
