ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Inquire around (for suitable bandages), then paint his hands to his neck, and keep his collarbones even, taking care against movement and dislocation, and let him sleep on his back; know that this fracture will be healed in thirty or thirty-five days, perhaps in twenty, according to the make-up and constitution of the patient.
de la brisure de la main	On the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and at the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather frequent dislocations.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient know how to cross himself, and sit upright before you evenly; then place his hand on an extended cloth, and have your assistants extend the broken bones, putting them in line with the mirror, until they are well aligned; apply a plaster cast and some swabs, if no abscess develops, then add a splint according to the size of the limb; it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the area of the hip joint, make a circular bandage and instruct the patient to wrap it tightly around their broken hip; then use a long piece of cloth, and let the heart-shaped pad be as big as the palm of your hand, and tie it in place as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you must place a pad above and another below at the hip joint, so that their hand remains open and straight, then tie everything around the hand, and secure the bandage between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of our fingers, be it the thumb, keep it equal, as is necessary; and secure it with the palm, and should you wish to place a small straight pad to lift the fracture, do not move it; and if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or any others, align them equally, and bind it with the healthy finger next to it; or you can bind all of them together forming an 'I', whichever works better, or place a pad above like for the thumb; and take care during restoration and when dealing with hot abscesses, and help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and this can be easily seen when the leg turns forwards or backwards; the restoration requires that one ligament be placed above the break, and another below it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each attendant extends their ligament to its equal place; this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the hip joint, one of the ligaments should be towards the wrist, and the other ligaments below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if the break is close to the knee, then the ligaments should be placed beside the knee, and the extension below; then let the attendants hold the bone in its equal place with both hands, until it returns to its natural shape, then apply the plaster and bind it, unless an abscess appears.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is hot abscess there, let it cool down before returning to your work and treatment; the binding is done in such manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap over the fracture with I hard bandage doubled in II or III layers, and let the excess remain; then turn the leg so that the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and thread I long wire between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the wire above; then turn the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place stars over the fracture, and put a star over the bone of the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the binding even, then start tying firmly III turns or IIII over the fracture; and as you go up from the fracture, tighten less; then take hold of I end of the wire that you have threaded between the leg and the thigh, and tie II stars that are above, then return below to the other end of the wire, until you reach near the foot; and bind it so that it does not move out of its place, then leave it like this, until no abscess or swelling nor any similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, so release it and treat what comes next, as we have said many times before; and if there are fragments of bone that grip, you must remove them, if possible; and if not, then the place must be split open, and pull forth with force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Sometimes the thigh is broken so that pins are inserted, as in the shoulder or arm; yet despite this restoration being done well, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thigh is healed in an L shape, or slightly less so, or more so, depending on the variety of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee alley there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or hole, which happens to all wounds, and unseen wounds, and one feels no pain.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	One restores it by placing what is round evenly with its two sides until they are assembled as well as can be done; then apply the plaster, and use a round splint if necessary, securing it as needed, then follow all arrangements we have mentioned for other breaks, just like hot abscesses and similar injuries; apply to each accident what is appropriate until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the breaking of the leg.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bone is broken, return to what came before.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is easily seen; return to beneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, promote extension, and make it even, binding the splinters equally; yet if the fracture is severe and there are many fragments, let the extension be lesser and lighter; ease according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that wrap the leg on either side, and are as long as the leg from knee to ankle; then layer with two bandages above and below, binding them in the middle too, so that the leg cannot bend right or left, and thus it is secure; some apply a brace of wood along the length of the leg, which holds it firm against movement, especially where there is an open wound in the fracture; move the leg each day to check for abscesses or other complications, and treat until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of broken bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breakage, but in the bones of the foot, there can be breaks and fractures, often just cracked in various places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breakage in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding from each other, have the patient put their foot on the ground, as if they are about to walk, then place your foot over theirs, where the bones are raised, press it until they return to their places; then apply a plaster cast and bandage it, placing underneath the sole of the foot a small board with two handles, then strap it to the foot appropriately, wrap it up with cloth bindings and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	Et when three days or four have passed, you may untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the toes broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place in the broken toe a rod according to its length, and slightly wider, then put beneath the foot that board I mentioned, and strain it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each toe a rod according to its measure, wrapped in a piece of linen cloth, and secure the board underneath the foot; and let it extend over the top of the board from outside the belly of the foot so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have mentioned regarding other fractures, as we have said before; and treat each accident appropriately.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone in the wrist.
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Have her sit with legs apart and lean toward the back part of her body, held from behind; then fill up the vagina-like opening in the nature of the patient's illness with cotton until it is as full as she is; then lift her upright slowly by lifting the hips little by little; when the cotton pops out to where it comes from the vagina, pull the bone along with a stick. When she wants to pee, take off the cotton, and put back in after pissing. Do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you want, take a goat bladder and tie one end of a cane into it; then blow strongly through the cane until the bladder is full inside; when that's done, return to nature by breaking down the fracture, fill it with cotton again and leave for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who applies their study and practice to them, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in many ways the right path of restoration; understand this, then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's windpipe and insert the penis into it; then wrap it in cloth around, and leave for three days like this, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	De brisure avec plaie (With breaks with wounds)
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one with breaks and wounds, especially if they are large, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, that they be treated now, as the treatments we have described attest.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply vitriol as a restraint, if you have nothing else, then begin again to repair the fracture that very hour or day, unless hot abscesses develop there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If hot abscesses appear there, leave the repair until the ninth day, so that the abscess is calm, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause an ill event to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the heart uncovered, you must put it in place lightly with your hands, using slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not available to match your hand's reach, draw it with this iron instrument which has seven or eight tines and is as long as the width of the wound; for this the surgeon must have three or four, depending on how many are needed in each fracture treatment; let them be round and a little thick so that they do not bend under compression on the limb being treated, and pointed at the end and wide halfway along like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called 'palainche', so the bent head must be placed on top of the protruding bone; push it once until it returns and is even with one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut away the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it away with an appropriate instrument, whether a scalpel or knife, to your ability; remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Make sure it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black styptic wine, and do so thoroughly if it's on the head; do not apply any kind of grease or ointment to the wound, as this will only cause infection and decay; afterwards administer stars (stitching?) once you have set the bone, leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around according to the size of the wound, making sure that it does not get trapped with the fracture; many times ignorant surgeons have done these things causing the patient to die or become corroded in some cases; and be more gentle than you would for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large and you fear an adverse event as we have mentioned earlier, and find pain in that place then one should not stitch it up; but instead use hard cloth around where the stitching would be done to wrap it up tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When after one or two days you see the wound suppurating, remove what you have placed on it and apply a healing ointment such as tetrafarmacum ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is firmly joined and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limb should be supported in such a way that the bowels move downward gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if after many days it remains unchanged and cannot heal but suppurates again, know that there are small bone fragments which must be sought out with a probe; remove all such pieces which cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms at the site or any other form of decay appears, then you must treat it according to what he said in his chapter before this one.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the thighbone or shoulder-blade, and other similar bones of large limbs, do not extract it because many times death results from doing so but rather let it rot leave it be until that happens; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days then treat the wound if you can, otherwise just leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	scabs that form on the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We are often consulted after the healing of fractures, especially when it is close to the joint and the disfigurement of the limb is noticeable; perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions properly.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, myrrh, and saracolic, acacia, and similar others; prepare any of these or all together with a styptic wine or with egg white or with honey; place this on the night in compresses and bind it tightly, without untying for two days; then disengage it, apply another dressing until knots are removed; you may also rub over a piece of well-prepared pumice stone; because the property of the pumice is to remove all swellings from members; if the knot has already hardened like stone and must be extracted, cut it open above with a razor; or shave away the superfluous parts that appear; or remove it with any kind of scraper until it is removed and cure it so that it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb which is weak after recovery.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and delicate, it happens due to many causes: one of which is that it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive drainage; or large movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is such that you make the patient eat, and soften their body so that blood multiplies within them; administer a bath to them, and give joy and rest; then apply ointment on the limb, so that the ointment draws in great nourishment, and frequently irrigate it with warm water until nourishment reaches the limb; and return to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The twisted limb after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bone is visibly protruding, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those fools who say that you must break the limb anew, and many foolish physicians have done this in our land; these practices are to be condemned as they lead to great harm and even death; however, if the swelling and inflammation are fresh, then they should be treated with warm water, or softening herbs can be boiled like mallow leaves, roots, and honeysuckle, along with similar things; apply a softening poultice such as dauco-lipon well made, or take the mucilage of mallow and mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil to make a poultice, or you may use boiled figs mixed with wheat bran, and other medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by continuously and extensively rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And provide gentle movements to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twistedness is hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, you must cut down to the bone, using subtle light incisions; then stitch and diligently treat the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, you must reset it immediately without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one waits too long, the joint swells up and might be forced back into place painfully; therefore it must not be moved while swollen: this often causes spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then leave him alone until the abscesses are healed; then bathe the limb with warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each joint as it returns to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations, from head to toe.
des mandibules	Of jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that jaws become dislocated on both sides, and this dislocation occurs in two ways: either they are slightly out of place and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and saliva pours from the mouth which cannot be held, nor can the mouth close, and speech is obscured by the tongue.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is minor, it returns through multiple arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and whole, you must reset it immediately without delay; in such a manner that the assistant holds the patient's head, and places one hand on their cheek close to the root of the dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation involves two parts; while the other hand should be outside to keep things even. Instruct the patient to relax their jaw and move it around freely in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	The assistant places [the hand] evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the resetting is difficult, especially when it involves both jaws together, bathe them with warm water and oil until they are loosened slightly for easier dislocation. Do not delay the process of resetting as we have instructed above.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's wound is well closed without softening, place on it moist dressings made of rosin oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on his back, and place two pillows under their head so that it doesn't move to the right or left, nor should they exert themselves in eating, but take light food until the pain is gone, and the jaws are unharmed; afterward, eat slowly what you wish, and do not strain to open your mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset to their proper place in one hour and are not returned to their positions, fever and regular chills will ensue, perhaps even diarrhea or vomiting of clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the one who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot be dislocated from the inner side near the neck or underarm, but it can sometimes be dislocated outwards and this is easily detected.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration method is to have the patient lie on their back often and stretch out their arms; then apply pressure with your palm firmly onto the affected area, and it will return; afterwards, place a poultice and bandage, securing it tightly; the shoulder which faces towards the neck cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it dislocates occasionally, put it back into place as we have described earlier; then apply the poultice and bandage, securing it tight; instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; likewise is the head of the shoulder restored when it becomes dislodged from its original position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	For the shoulder dislocation.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: first, it dislocates at the lower part of the socket underneath; secondly, it dislocates on the back side; and rarely it dislocates above, which happens less often; and it does not dislocate behind due to the shoulder, nor inside because of nerves. It often dislocates below towards the socket, especially in those with little flesh, as it falls out quickly for them; for those with enough flesh, it falls out with difficulty and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And it happens to some men that there is a blow or breakage, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	The dislocations are known when it falls towards the armpit, creating a gap between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, with an obvious difference; you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and beneath the armpit when touching the head of the shoulder, like an egg; the patient cannot return their hand to their nose nor move in any way; if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden as you can feel it clearly upon touch; this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset, whether new or if the child is affected.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the assistants to lift the patient's hand upwards and then place your fists beneath the armpit, lifting the joint with force back into its place; the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upwards while putting it underneath; this will bring relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not go as we have said in a few days, the patient must be bathed in warm water; and administer to him gently softening and soothing medicines, such as decoctions of althea, fenugreek, and mellilot in water, and let it be administered; then remind the patient on his back, and place under the shoulder a cushion of wool that is even, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the heel of the patient's hand on the cushion, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the patient's hand; and have another minister hold the patient's head so it does not move downwards; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you wish to reset it according to this method: and make sure that there is present a man who is larger than the patient; and he should be on the right side of the patient's body, and push the patient's shoulder under his armpit, and lift the arm up so that the patient hangs in the air; while another minister pulls the patient's hand downwards towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, you may use something heavy with them, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	You may also reset it in another way: have a long pole firmly planted in the ground, so that the shoulder is as straight as an arrow, and not too thick nor too thin; then place it beneath the patient, but let there be soft cloth underneath, and let the patient stretch along the length of the pole; then extend their hand downwards on the other side very carefully, and the joint will return to its place little by little; if it does not wish to return despite all these things we have said, then do this cure: take a pole two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a rounded head so you can fit it perfectly underneath the shoulder-blade, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay upon the head of the injured person a damp cloth so that it will not hurt them, then place them underneath the sick person's bench; and extend their arm along the length of the wooden shaft, and bind the shoulder to the wood, and attach the arm to the top of the main pole, then put one of the arms on a prop of an upright from the wide side, and let the hand hang down, and leave the rest of the body hanging: the joint should now be in place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, no matter how, you must then put underneath the bench a round pad of equal wool, then apply the plaster prepared with mill-powder, together with incense and egg-white, all over the shoulder and around it, then tighten the bandage underneath the bench accordingly, and turn the tie on top of the plaster, embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands stay in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he must eat little, so that the limb is strengthened, for then it will heal more quickly; and then increase his diet after five or seven days, and move him; and if it is firm and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place due to moisture or any other reason, you must apply cauterization to three points as described before in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut, stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be properly fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the armpit, and breasts, or at the back, is caused by a push, and stretching of hands, and it should be treated in another place; treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process there is cracking in the limb, and it moves slowly, the patient should bathe frequently until this cracking subsides and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the shoulder dislocation...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the shoulder joint is repeatedly dislocated and returns to its place; if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected because it can be clearly seen and felt; it will dislocate according to each person's specific anatomy.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick person's cut with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm or reach their shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before any abscesses form, because if an abscess forms, it would be difficult to reset; and sometimes it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, causing even more pain, and death may occur as a result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such that you can reset it by extending their arm with both your hands; and spread their arms, placing your hands around theirs to guide them accordingly towards the cut, above and below, and push the joint back together at the palms or at the wrist until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it occurs when one's hand doubles over against their own hand, and pressure should be applied to the base of the palm which has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; with one person extending the arm, and another bending it, so that no movement is possible during the extension; then turn the arm in both directions, having previously wrapped a long and wide piece of cloth around it; once you have joined the joint back together with your hand, apply some oil to soften the joint, then press down on the joint firmly until it returns. Once it is back in place, apply dry poultice made from egg white onto the wound, strain this firmly, then bend the arm up against the patient's neck, leaving for several days before removing the binding.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and leave it alone; but if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the poultice and bandage, leaving it for a few days until it is securely in position; then you may untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if the patient feels a cracking sensation after the joint is reset and it moves again, bathe and gently rub the area, pressing until it is eased; or apply to the joint a dressing of fatty sheep's wool, leaving it on for a day and night, then remove it, and place the limb in a warm bath; when sweating, gently rub the joint, then reapply the dressing, followed by another warm bath; repeat this two or three times until it is healed; if you wish to, apply moist cow manure warmed with butter onto the area, strapping it on; they will return to their proper state.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The wrist is dislocated, and its return is light compared to other joints However, one must reset it immediately while it is still dislocated before the area swells or becomes hot with abscesses.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And to reset it you place the injured hand on a table and your assistants stretch out that hand, aligning the gaze with their palm so they push until it returns Then make sure that it is indeed in its proper place by having the patient lay the back of their hand flat on a table as well as when stretching.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand then have the patient lay their hand flat on the table, back facing up, and you place your own hand over theirs onto that joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; if not, strain the soothing emollient plasters for hot abscesses and leave them like this without beginning again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint will remain dislocated; this does no harm to the patient while the hand is relaxed and cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves or arteries are severed; unless there is another method of grasping nearby with a cautery, perhaps nothing else will work.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we mentioned, then strain and leave it for five days, then unravel and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they cannot move it well, and there is some damage, then bathe them in warm water, and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the finger of the hand is dislocated on every side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the belly; then extend the finger and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is disjoined; leave it for two days, and then make it equal that day; bind it at night as we have said, and release it during the day, moving it, and rebind it at night; do this often until it becomes narrow, and also do likewise if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, performing as you have done before until it heals; and do all the same when it is dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine from the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that flatus escapes without control, one cannot hold it in, and often some members become weak, such as both thighs or arms, or sometimes the spine shifts into four parts; this shifting of the spine to the rear is called "gilbositez": its treatment is that you must turn if gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure or healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, the old methods of treatment say there is not much benefit in all this; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention and made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hump that develops on the chest front, there is no cure or relief; and likewise, the one that appears directly on both sides, and cannot be treated except for the one that arises on the back, as I mentioned; it's necessary that the patient lie down on his face in a level place, with a strainer under him, so he doesn't get hurt; then stick one poker at the head firmly into the ground, and another at the feet, tie a rope over the shoulders of the sick person, and attach another to the hips, knees, and ankles; two assistants know how to tie ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two pokers; they should be well secured, the poker as we have said, and the doctors place their palms on the spine firmly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return through this cure, take a board of III arms in length and place it under the wall, let the patient be on their side, insert the head of the board underneath the wall, then put the middle of the board onto the spine; have those who are assisting place their feet on the other end of the board, press hard until it returns to its place; if you wish, do this in a twist that turns toward the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Stick II posts in the patient's head an arm's length apart and two others near their feet, with a span of space between each post; have one hole in each post where the rope runs through, and make sure these are firmly anchored into the ground so they do not move; for every pair of posts, insert another turning post above them, around which the ropes will twist, and include two small posts at this pivot point that span a palm's length to assist with the turning; now tie one end of the rope between the shoulder blades to the twisting rope near the head, and attach the other rope towards the feet on the opposite side to another twisting post, and have each assistant turn their own rope until it is tight around the spine in an even manner as we described.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d'uef, et puis les estoupes, and puis l'estele d'une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l'espondile sainne, puis le lie d'un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu'il soit sanez; et s'aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l'estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c'est li os qui apert, por coi on n'i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.
des dislocations de la hainche	The dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that only dislocations cause damage to the hip joints and shoulder joints, not like with other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: internally and externally, and anteriorly and posteriorly; it is more often dislocated internally, but rarely anteriorly or posteriorly.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its internal dislocation is that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the sick person's knee sticks out more than the healthy one, and they cannot bend their unhealthy knee forward; and the area next to this is swollen from a hot abscess because the thigh bone has come loose.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes after default is such that these accidents are contrary to what came before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it happens beforehand are that he stretches out his leg according to its completion; nevertheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wishes to make him walk, he cannot proceed, and retains his urine, and his veins swell, and when he goes, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it happens behind are that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the femur is in place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The recovery from this type of dislocation is such that you must wait if the dislocation is old and remains in its position according to its condition, for there is no treatment; and it ought not be presumed upon.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for someone with a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, you must act quickly to return the joint, stretching it inward and outward, and moving it right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return with this method, you must prepare one strong assistant and have them grasp the leg firmly with both hands or bind it above the knee with a strap; another assistant should place their hands underneath his armpits and then tightly tie a cord around his thigh; another holds the end of the cord; all three assistants stretch simultaneously upwards and downwards until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, remaining suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must treat it similarly. When dislocations are in the thigh, you must lay the patient on their healthy side, then tie a bandage around the root of the thigh, and the place below the groin, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the groin, and towards the hip; another assistant should take his arms, embrace the upper part of the sick thigh, and extend it forcibly outwards: it will return to its place now; and this kind of dislocation is less serious than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have described, then you must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong soft bandage over their heels and knees, and let the sick leg be extended twice as much as the other; then hang him from the head of a pole, and have it suspended two arms' length above the ground; then instruct one assistant to embrace the head of the thigh, and another assistant hanging alongside the patient, who should firmly embrace the thigh, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is external, so lies the patient, as we have said in reference to the one with curvature, bind the ligament above the sick leg tightly, and also on the foot; then place two hot irons, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert an iron between the patient's thighs into the joint; and have moistened cloths planted around it so that they do not burn the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and let the examiner hold equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not, place him on a table, and press as we have said for curvature, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	Et when the dislocations are in front, it is necessary to stretch the sick leg completely, and according to what I have said; and let the examiners place their weight on top of the affected angle, then push with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are on the outside, it is not necessary to stretch the affected leg downwards or lift it off the ground, instead, it should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outwards, as we have mentioned about the position lying on two hips; and let him be on his face, with the binding extended as previously stated, and press on the joint onto the table; this will be sufficient when the patient stretches his legs, and they are equal in length; then adjust the thighs, apply an ointment, and wrap it firmly with a bandage so that the hip does not move; let him rest for three or four days, then release the binding, and reapply the plaster; if you see that the legs are now even, bind them as before, and leave this for three days; then release again, and have him walk gently until his limbs regain their strength.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knees dislocate in three ways: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg towards their thigh, and if it does not reach their thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and stretch their leg if they can, and place your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your two hands, then bend the two sides of the knee sharply; and another assistant stretches their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can gently touch their leg to their thigh; and apply a plaster cast on top, and make them stretch the leg towards the thigh, and keep it bound together strongly for three or four days, then release it; and do not let the patient walk until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, apply strong extension as we have mentioned in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Sometimes the heel is partially displaced, and sometimes fully dislocated, internally or externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The signs are that the ankle is swollen and more so in the part where it is dislocated; the reset is light, and one must gently extend it with their hands when it is only partially displaced.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.
